المتصفح لكتب التراجم يجد تاريخين لمولد السعد، والاختلاف في تاريخ ولادة الأعلام ووفاتهم، يكاد يكون ظاهرة عامة لا يخلو منها كتاب من كتب التراجم . فمثلا صاحب الترجمة التي بين أيدينا . يذكر عنه طاشكبري (١) زاده أنه ولد في صفر سنة ٧٢٢ هـ وهذا التاريخ يؤكده طاشكبري زاده لأنه نقله عن فتح الله الشرواني تلميذ التفتازاني والذي ذكر في أوائل شرحه لكتاب أستاذه (الإرشاد) أنه زار مرقده بسرخس فوجد مكتوباً عليه ولد عليه الرحمة والرضوان في صفر سنة ۷۲۲ هـ ) ويؤيد هذا التاريخ أيضاً الذي ذكره فتح الله الشرواني أنه وجد مكتوباً على ظهر بعض نسخ المطول، وينقل هذا عن صاحب (روضات الجنات) (۲) حيث يقول إن هذا التاريخ وجدته على بعض نسخ المطول القديمة، ويوافقه أيضاً الشيخ البهائي فيقول : ولد العلامة التفتازاني في صفر سنة ٧٢٢هـ وتوفي سنة ٧٩٢هـ فكان عمره ٧٠ سنة. ويؤكد هذا التاريخ الإمام البغدادي في (هدية العارفين) (۳) والشوكاني في (البدر الطالع ) (٤) ، والكنوي في (كتائب(٥) أعلام الأخيار). ودائرة المعارف (٦) الإسلامية وأرمنيوس فنبري في (تاريخ بخاری)(۷). وهناك رأي آخر يتزعمه ابن حجر في كتابه (الدرر الكامنة) (۲) حيث يقرر أنه ولد سنة ٧١٢ هـ ويقول : إن هذا ما وجد بخط ابن الجزري، ونقل عنه هذا التاريخ الإمام السيوطي في كتابه بغية الوعاة) (۳) ، وابن العماد في (شذرات (٤) الذهب). وذكره أيضاً ابن تغرى بردى في (المنهل (٥) الصافي ) .. هنا تأتي حيرة الباحث المدقق، ويتساءل بينه وبين نفسه : أي الرأيين أقرب إلى الصواب؟ وأيهما يرجح؟ لأن الاختيار في مثل هذه الحالة، أو الترجيح بين الآراء لا يتم في العادة إلا من خلال أدلة قوية، ترجح أحد القولين على الآخر، ونحن نميل إلى ترجيح الرأي الأول اعتماداً على ما ذكر في كثير من كتب التراجم أن أول كتاب ألفه السعد هو كتاب شرح التصريف. وكان عمره آنذاك ست عشرة سنة، وكان ذلك سنة ٧٣٨هـ ، وكذلك ذكر الخونسارى. أن سعد الدين شرع في تأليف شرحه المطول على التلخيص في أواسط سنة ٧٤٢هـ ، وفرغ منه سنة ٧٤٨هـ . وقال : وكان عمره حين الشروع عشرين سنة، وهذا كله يؤكد أن مولده كان سنة ٧٢٢هـ ، وأيما كان الأمر، فلقد ولد التفتازاني، وعاش عيشة ممتدة طويلة بلغت السبعين عاماً، قام فيها بأعمـال خالدة، وترك فيها بصماته المضيئة المنيرة على جبهة التاريخ، وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، فكيف كانت نشأته ..؟
The one who examines books of biographies finds two dates for the birth of al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani), and disagreement about the birth date and death date of notable figures is almost a general phenomenon from which no book of biographies is free. For example, the subject of our biography: Tashkubri Zadah mentions about him that he was born in Safar of the year 722 AH, and this date is confirmed by Tashkubri Zadah because he transmitted it from Fathallah al-Shirwani, the student of al-Taftazani, who mentioned in the beginning of his commentary on his teacher's book (al-Irshad) that he visited his grave in Sarakhs and found written on it: 'May mercy and good pleasure be upon him, born in Safar of the year 722 AH.' This date is also supported by what Fathallah al-Shirwani mentioned, that he found it written on the back of some copies of al-Mutawwal, and he transmits this from the author of Rawdat al-Jannat, where he says: 'I found this date on some old copies of al-Mutawwal.' Sheikh al-Baha'i also agrees with it, saying: 'The distinguished scholar al-Taftazani was born in Safar of the year 722 AH and died in the year 792 AH, so his age was 70 years.' This date is confirmed by Imam al-Baghdadi in Hadiyyat al-'Arifin, al-Shawkani in al-Badr al-Tali', al-Kanawi in Kata'ib A'lam al-Akhyar, the Encyclopedia of Islam, and Arminius Vambery in History of Bukhara. There is another opinion led by Ibn Hajar in his book al-Durar al-Kamina, where he asserts that he was born in the year 712 AH and says: 'This is what was found in the handwriting of Ibn al-Jazari.' This date was transmitted from him by Imam al-Suyuti in his book Bughyat al-Wu'ah, Ibn al-'Imad in Shadharat al-Dhahab, and also mentioned by Ibn Taghribirdi in al-Manhal al-Safi. Here comes the confusion of the meticulous researcher, and he wonders to himself: Which of the two opinions is closer to correctness? And which one is more likely? Because choosing in such a situation, or weighing between opinions, is usually not done except through strong evidence that favors one of the two statements over the other. And we lean towards preferring the first opinion, based on what is mentioned in many books of biographies: that the first book authored by al-Sa'd was the book Sharh al-Tasrif, and he was then sixteen years old, and that was in the year 738 AH. Likewise, al-Khunsari mentioned that Sa'd al-Din began authoring his commentary al-Mutawwal on al-Talkhis in the middle of the year 742 AH and finished it in the year 748 AH. He said: 'He was twenty years old at the beginning.' And all of this confirms that his birth was in the year 722 AH. And whatever the case, al-Taftazani was born and lived a long, extended life that reached seventy years, during which he accomplished immortal works and left his bright, luminous imprints on the forehead of history. And if that is so, how was his upbringing?
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a biographical discussion about the birth year of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The author begins by noting that disagreement over birth and death dates is common in biographical sources. He then presents two conflicting reports. The first report, supported by many authorities, states that al-Taftazani was born in Safar 722 AH. The author lists the chain of transmission: Tashkubri Zadah quotes Fathallah al-Shirwani, a student of al-Taftazani, who saw an inscription on his grave in Sarakhs with that date. Additional support comes from notes on old copies of al-Mutawwal, and the opinions of al-Bahai, al-Baghdadi, al-Shawkani, and others. The second report, championed by Ibn Hajar and followed by al-Suyuti, Ibn al-'Imad, and Ibn Taghribirdi, gives the year 712 AH, citing the handwriting of Ibn al-Jazari. The author then expresses the researcher's dilemma and states his preference for the first opinion (722 AH). The primary evidence is the dating of al-Taftazani's early works: his first book, Sharh al-Tasrif, was written at age 16 in 738 AH, which would place his birth around 722 AH (since 738 - 16 = 722). Similarly, his commentary al-Mutawwal was begun at age 20 in 742 AH, also consistent with a 722 birth. The author concludes that this evidence confirms the 722 date, emphasizing that regardless of the exact year, al-Taftazani lived about seventy years and left a lasting legacy. The passage ends with a rhetorical transition to his upbringing.

?

The Birth Year of al-Taftazani: Weighing the Evidence
Author compares two opinions on Taftazani's birth year and gives evidence for his preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars use biographical evidence to resolve disagreements about historical figures' birth years.

Core Idea
Biographical details like age at writing first book can confirm birth years.

Biographical accounts sometimes disagree on basic facts like a scholar's birth year. In this passage, the author examines two conflicting opinions about the birth year of the great scholar Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. He then presents evidence from his earliest works to support one opinion over the other. As you read, notice how the author builds his argument using multiple sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions
Read the passage and note the two different birth years mentioned (712 AH and 722 AH) and who supports each.
The first opinion is attributed to George Zaidan, the second to Ibn Hajar and others.
2
Examine the evidence
Look for the specific evidence the author provides to prefer one opinion. He cites the age at which al-Taftazani wrote his first book and his commentary.
3
Evaluate the argument
Consider how the author uses these ages to calculate the birth year. For example, if he was 16 in 738 AH, his birth year would be 722 AH.
This is a simple subtraction exercise.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author ends with a rhetorical question about al-Taftazani's upbringing. Think about why this matters for understanding the scholar's life.
It suggests his youth and early achievements.

Commentary
This passage presents the scholarly debate about al-Taftazani's birth year. The author then expresses the perplexity of the researcher and explains that preference between opinions requires strong evidence. The author provides evidence: al-Taftazani wrote his first book Sharh al-Tasrif at age 16 in 738 AH, which would place his birth in 722 AH. Also, al-Khunsari notes that he began his commentary on al-Talkhis at age 20 in 742 AH, also pointing to 722 AH. The author concludes that his birth year is 722 AH, and he lived to about 70. B) The age he wrote his first book and his commentary on al-Talkhis

D) The opinion of George Zaidan alone

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's birth year is best established as 722 AH based on his age when he authored his first works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author carefully weighed evidence from multiple sources to determine a birth year. When you encounter conflicting reports about Islamic knowledge, do you instinctively prefer the most famous opinion, or do you actively seek corroborating evidence? What steps can you take to verify what you learn?
?
Taftazani authored his first book at 16. At your current age, are you prioritizing deepening your knowledge of sacred sciences? If not, what concrete change will you make this week to invest your time in seeking beneficial knowledge?

Taftazani's Birthplace and the Naming of Nasa
Taftazani's birthplace and the naming of Nasa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Taftazani's place of birth and the historical anecdote behind the name of the city of Nasa.

Core Idea
A city's name can preserve a story of conquest and mercy.

This lesson opens the biography of al-Taftazani with his origins. We learn that he was born in a small village called Taftazan, which belonged to the city of Nasa in Khurasan. The author then shares a remarkable story about how Nasa got its name, linking it to the Islamic conquests. This background sets the stage for understanding the cultural and intellectual world into which Taftazani was born.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage that describes Taftazani's birthplace and the etymology of Nasa. Pay attention to the reason for naming.
The passage includes a historical anecdote.
2
Identify the location
Note the place: Taftazan village, Nasa city, Khurasan region. Locate it on a mental map.
Surrounding cities are Sarakhs, Marw, Nishapur.
3
Understand the etymology
Understand the story: When Muslims came, only women remained, so they called it Nasa (from 'nisa' = women).
The nisba is Nasa'i or Nasawi.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how historical events shape place names and what this tells us about Islamic conquests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأته
ولد التفتازاني بقرية تفتازان التابعة لمدينة (نسا) وهي مدينة بخراسان. تحيط بها سرخس ومرو ونيشابور، ويعلل العلماء سبب تسميتها بهذا الاسم أن المسلمين لما وردوا خراسان قصدوها فبلغ أهلها أخبار الجيش المغير الفاتح، فهربوا، ولم يتخلف بها غير النساء، فلما أتاها المسلمون لم يجدوا فيها رجلاً واحداً فقالوا: هؤلاء نساء والنساء لا يقاتلن فننسى أمرها الآن إلى أن يعود رجالهن فتركوها ومضوا فسميت بذلك (نسا) والنسبة الصحيحة إليها (نسائي) وقيل نسوي أيضاً.
وهذه المدينة كانت ملتقى أبناء المسلمين النازحين إليها لحفظ القرآن، والتفقه في أمور الدين، ولقد ترك التفتازاني قريته الصغيرة، ورحل إلى (نسا) ولا ندري كم من الأعوام قضاها في تلك المدينة؟، ولا الحلقات الأولى التي تلقى فيها قواعد الخط، وإملاء الكتابة واستظهار القرآن، والتفقه في أمور الدين.
لا شك أنه عاش فيها فترة يهملها التاريخ تماماً، حتى يحدثنا ابن العماد الحنبلي بأنه يترك (نسا) وينتقل فجأة إلى سمرقند، ويظهر ظهوراً بارعاً في حلقة طلاب كبار، ودعوا عهد الطفولة، وأخذوا يعبون من المعرفة عباً، العضد ويصاولون أستاذهم في أقيسة أرسطو، وشذرات ابن سينا، وتهويمات الفارابي في مدينته الفاضلة ويصبون اللعنات على أفلاطون لقوله بنظرية العقول
His Upbringing: Al-Taftazani was born in the village of Taftazan, belonging to the city of (Nasa), which is a city in Khurasan. Surrounding it are Sarakhs, Marw, and Nishapur. The scholars explain the reason for its naming as such: when the Muslims came to Khurasan, they headed towards it. The news of the conquering invading army reached its inhabitants, so they fled, and none remained behind except the women. When the Muslims arrived, they did not find a single man, so they said: 'These are women, and women do not fight. Let us postpone this matter now until their men return.' So they left it and moved on. Thus it was named (Nasa). The correct nisba to it is (Nasa'i), and it is also said Nasawi. This city was a meeting place for Muslim sons who migrated to it to memorize the Quran and gain understanding in religious matters. Al-Taftazani left his small village and travelled to (Nasa), and we do not know how many years he spent in that city, nor the first circles in which he learned the rules of calligraphy, dictation of writing, memorization of the Quran, and understanding of religious matters. There is no doubt that he lived there a period completely neglected by history, until Ibn al-‘Imad al-Hanbali tells us that he left (Nasa) and suddenly moved to Samarkand, and he appeared brilliantly in a circle of senior students who had left behind childhood and were drinking deeply from knowledge, ‘al-‘Adud? and they were debating with their teacher in the syllogisms of Aristotle, the fragments of Ibn Sina, the fantasies of al-Farabi in his virtuous city, and they were cursing Plato for his theory of intellects.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of al-Taftazani's early life. It begins with his birthplace: the village of Taftazan near the city of Nasa in Khurasan. The author then digresses to explain the origin of the name 'Nasa', giving an anecdote about the Muslim conquest: only women were left, so the Muslims spared the city and called it 'Nasa' (from 'nisa' meaning women). The correct nisba is 'Nasa'i' or 'Nasawi'. Then the author notes that Nasa was a center for Islamic learning, attracting students. Al-Taftazani left his village for Nasa, but his early education there is not recorded. Historical silence surrounds his early years until Ibn al-‘Imad reports that he suddenly moved to Samarkand, where he emerged as a brilliant student among advanced scholars. The passage ends with a vivid description of the scholarly circle: they debated Aristotelian logic, Ibn Sina's works, al-Farabi's political philosophy, and criticized Plato's theory of intellects. This illustrates the intellectual environment in which al-Taftazani matured.

Key Terms
تفتازان
نسا
خراسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the city was named after a person or a geographical feature.
Correction: The name comes from the Arabic word for women (nisa) because only women were left when the Muslims arrived.

Checkpoint
What explanation does the passage give for the name 'Nasa'?
A) It was named after a founder called Nasa
B) It means 'rocky plain' in Persian
C) When Muslims came, only women remained, so they called it Nasa from 'nisa'
D) It is named after a nearby river

Key Takeaway
The city of Nasa received its name from a historical event when only women remained to greet the Muslim army.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where someone appears weak or defenseless, do you show restraint and mercy like the Muslim army, or do you exploit their vulnerability? This lesson records an act of mercy that became a city's name. What would your name be remembered for if your actions today were etched into history?
?
The Muslims postponed judgment and left. Is there someone in your life you have been too quick to judge or condemn? How can you apply the lesson of 'let us postpone this matter' to give them a chance, and what would that look like practically?
?
The city's name, Nasa, is a permanent reminder of the mercy shown to women. What permanent marks are you leaving on the lives of others through your words and actions? Are they marks of mercy or harshness, and what do they reveal about your iman?

Taftazani's Early Education and Move to Samarkand
Taftazani's early education and intellectual leap to Samarkand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early educational context of al-Taftazani and his transition to the advanced scholarly circle in Samarkand.

Core Idea
History often overlooks early years, but a scholar's true mettle emerges in advanced debate.

After establishing his birthplace, the passage turns to Taftazani's early education. It notes that Nasa was a hub for Quran memorization and religious study. Taftazani left his village for Nasa, but the details of his early learning are lost to history. Then, Ibn al-‘Imad reports that he suddenly moved to Samarkand, where he joined a circle of advanced students who engaged vigorously with Aristotelian logic, Ibn Sina, al-Farabi, and even criticized Plato. This lesson explores that intellectual leap.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the second half of the biography focusing on Taftazani's move and the scholarly circle.
Notice the description: they debated Aristotle, Ibn Sina, al-Farabi, and cursed Plato.
2
Identify the educational gap
Note the author's admission: history does not record Taftazani's early years in Nasa.
This is a common gap in medieval biographies.
3
Visualize the Samarkand circle
Imagine the scene: senior students debating logic, philosophy, and criticizing Plato's theory of intellects.
This shows the intellectual rigor of the era.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider what this tells us about Taftazani's environment and how it shaped his thought.

The Birthplace of al-Taftazani and the Story of Nasa
Anecdote about the naming of Nasa and al-Taftazani's birthplace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Nasa as al-Taftazani's hometown and the historical anecdote behind its name.

Core Idea
A city's name can carry a story: Nasa, the city of women.

Our study of al-Taftazani begins with his origins. This lesson introduces his birthplace, the city of Nasa in Khurasan, and a curious story about how it got its name. The anecdote reflects the early Islamic conquests and the local tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the first paragraph
Read the Arabic passage describing al-Taftazani's birthplace and the anecdote of Nasa. Notice the narrative style.
The story explains why the city was named Nasa.
2
Understand the anecdote
Consider why the Muslims named the city Nasa. Reflect on the meaning of the word and the historical context.
3
Learn the correct nisba
Note the correct relative adjective (nisba) for Nasa: 'Nasai' or 'Nasawi'.
This is important for identifying scholars from this city.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأته
ولد التفتازاني بقرية تفتازان التابعة لمدينة (نسا) وهي مدينة بخراسان . تحيط بها سرخس ومرو ونیسابور، ويعلل العلماء سبب تسميتها بهذا الاسم أن المسلمين لما وردوا خراسان قصدوها فبلغ أهلها أخبار الجيش المغير الفاتح فهربوا، ولم يتخلف بها غير النساء، فلما أتاها المسلمون لم يجدوا فيها رجلاً واحداً فقالوا: هؤلاء نساء والنساء لا يقاتلن فننسى أمرها الآن إلى أن يعود رجالهن فتركوها ومضوا فسميت بذلك (نسا) والنسبة الصحيحة إليها (نسائي) وقيل نسوي أيضاً.
وهذه المدينة كانت ملتقى أبناء المسلمين النازحين إليها لحفظ القرآن والتفقه في أمور الدين، ولقد ترك التفتازاني قريته الصغيرة ورحل إلى (نسا) ولا ندري كم من الأعوام قضاها في تلك المدينة؟ ولا الحلقات الأولى التي تلقى فيها قواعد الخط وإملاء الكتابة واستظهار القرآن والتفقه في أمور الدين؟
لا شك أنه عاش فيها فترة يهملها التاريخ تماماً حتى يحدثنا ابن العماد الحنبلي بأنه يترك (نسا) وينتقل فجأة إلى سمرقند ويظهر ظهوراً بارعاً في حلقة طلاب كبار ودعوا عهد الطفولة وأخذوا يعبون من المعرفة عباً، ويصاولون أستاذهم في أقيسة أرسطو وشذرات ابن سينا وتهويمات الفارابي في مدينته الفاضلة ويصبون اللعنات على أفلاطون لقوله بنظرية العقول العشرة.
كم بقي التفتازاني في سمرقند؟ إننا لا نكاد نعلم شيئاً عن الفترة الأولى التي قضاها في سمرقند حتى إذا كان عام ٧٤٢هـ ينتقل فجأة إلى جرجانية وهي مدينة عظيمة على شاطىء نهر جيحون وأهل خوارزم يسمونها بلسانهم كر كانج فعربت إلى الجرجانية. يصفها صاحب معجم البلدان بأنها أعظم المدن التي رآها وأكثرها أموالاً وأحسنها أحوالاً.
دخل التفتازاني هذه المدينة وهو عالم كبير تسبقه شهرته لشرحه کتاب التصريف للزنجاني ولقد أعجبه المقام في هذه المدينة وعكف على التأليف والتصنيف وأصبح له طلاب وتلاميذ يتسابقون إليه ويجنون الثمار من بين يديه وفيها أتم كتابه (المطول على التلخيص).
ما كاد يهل عام ٧٤٨هـ حتى قرر الرحيل من الجرجانية إلى بلدة (هراة) وهي مدينة عظيمة مشهورة من أمهات مدن خراسان فيها بساتين كثيرة ومياه غزيرة وخيرات وفيرة حتى قال شاعرها أحمد السامي الهروي:
هراة أرض خصبها واسع ونبتها اللقاح والنرجس ما أحد منها إلى غيرها يخرج إلا بعد ما يفلس
ويقول الأديب البارع الزوزني:
هراة أردت مقامي بها لشتى فضائلها الوافرة الشمال وأعنابها وأعين غزلانها الساحرة
وكانت (هراة) في ذلك مملوءة بالعلماء وبأهل الفضل والحكمة ومساجدها تضج بالمناقشات العلمية وصولات العلماء ومختلف الآراء والأفكار ومن علماء (هراة) الحسين بن إدريس الهروي المحدث روى عنه ابن حبان. وللحسين هذا كتاب في التاريخ صنفه على حروف المعجم.
إلى هذه المدينة التي تموج بكل أنواع الحياة ألقى السعد رحله فيها وكان يتأبط كتابه الضخم المطول على التلخيص والذي كتبه في جرجانية فأهداه إلى ملك (هراة) معز الدين أبو الحسين بمجرد دخوله إلى المدينة.
His upbringing
Al-Taftazani was born in the village of Taftazan, belonging to the city of Nasa, which is a city in Khurasan. Surrounding it are Sarakhs, Marw, and Nishapur. Scholars explain the reason for its naming by this name: that when the Muslims came to Khurasan, they headed toward it, and its inhabitants learned of the news of the conquering army, so they fled, and none remained in it but the women. When the Muslims arrived, they did not find a single man there, so they said: 'These are women, and women do not fight, so we will postpone its matter until their men return.' So they left it and went on, thus it was named Nasa. The correct relative adjective to it is Nasai, and it is also said Nasawi.
This city was a meeting place for the sons of Muslims who migrated to it for memorizing the Quran and gaining understanding in matters of religion. Al-Taftazani left his small village and traveled to Nasa, and we do not know how many years he spent in that city, nor the first circles in which he received the rules of handwriting, dictation of writing, memorization of the Quran, and understanding in matters of religion.
There is no doubt that he lived in it for a period that history completely neglects, until Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali tells us that he leaves Nasa and suddenly moves to Samarkand and appears brilliantly in the circle of older students who have left childhood behind and drink deeply of knowledge, and they wrestle with their teacher in Aristotle's syllogisms, Ibn Sina's fragments, al-Farabi's fantasies in his Virtuous City, and they heap curses on Plato for his theory of the ten intellects.
How long did al-Taftazani remain in Samarkand? We hardly know anything about the first period he spent in Samarkand until the year 742 AH, when he suddenly moves to Jurjaniyya, which is a great city on the bank of the Jayhun River. The people of Khwarazm call it in their language 'Kar Kang', which was Arabized to al-Jurjaniyya. The author of Mu'jam al-Buldan describes it as the greatest city he had seen, the wealthiest in resources, and the best in conditions.
Al-Taftazani entered this city, a great scholar preceded by his reputation for his commentary on al-Zanjani's book al-Tasrif. He was pleased with staying in this city and devoted himself to authorship and composition. He acquired students and disciples who raced to him and harvested the fruits from his hands. In it he completed his book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis.
Hardly had the year 748 AH begun when he decided to travel from Jurjaniyya to the town of Herat, a great and famous city, one of the mother cities of Khurasan. It has many gardens, abundant waters, and plentiful bounties, so much so that its poet Ahmad al-Sami al-Harawi said:
Herat is a land whose fertility is vast, its plants are the pollen and the narcissus. No one leaves it for another except after going bankrupt.
And the accomplished adib al-Zawzani says:
Herat, I desired my stay in it for the sake of various abundant virtues: the north wind, its grapes, and the captivating eyes of its gazelles.
And Herat at that time was filled with scholars, people of virtue and wisdom. Its mosques teemed with scientific discussions and the assaults of scholars and various opinions and ideas. Among the scholars of Herat was al-Husayn ibn Idris al-Harawi, the hadith scholar, from whom Ibn Hibban narrated. This al-Husayn has a book on history arranged alphabetically.
To this city, teeming with all kinds of life, al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) cast his saddle, carrying his great book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis, which he had written in Jurjaniyya, and he presented it to the king of Herat, Mu'izz al-Din Abu al-Husayn, as soon as he entered the city.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative detailing the early life and scholarly travels of al-Taftazani, the author of Sharh al-Maqasid. It begins by noting his birthplace in the village of Taftazan, part of the city of Nasa in Khurasan. The author provides an anecdote about the naming of Nasa: when Muslims first arrived, the men fled, leaving only women, so the name Nasa was derived from 'nisa' (women). He then notes the correct nisba (relative adjective) is 'Nasai' or 'Nasawi'.
The passage explains that Nasa was a center for Quran memorization and religious learning, and al-Taftazani left his village to study there. The details of his early education are unknown. He then moved to Samarkand, where he joined advanced students engaging in debates on Aristotelian logic, Ibn Sina's philosophy, and al-Farabi's ideas, as well as criticizing Plato's theory of ten intellects.
The narrative continues with his move to Jurjaniyya in 742 AH, a city on the Jayhun River with great wealth. He was already renowned for his commentary on al-Zanjani's al-Tasrif. In Jurjaniyya, he devoted himself to writing and teaching, completing his major work al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis.
In 748 AH, he relocated to Herat, praised poetically for its fertility and beauty. Herat was a center of learning, with scholars like al-Husayn ibn Idris al-Harawi. Al-Taftazani presented his al-Mutawwal to the ruler Mu'izz al-Din Abu al-Husayn upon arrival. The passage thus covers his geographical and intellectual journey, highlighting his growing reputation and scholarly output.

Key Takeaway
Nasa was named after the women left behind, and its people are called Nasai or Nasawi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the Muslims arrived in Nasa and found only women, they said, 'These are women, and women do not fight, so we will postpone its matter until their men return.' How does this action reflect the Islamic principle of protecting the vulnerable? In your own interactions, how can you show similar consideration for those who are defenseless?
?
The city was named Nasa after the women who were left behind. Think of a person or group in your life who often goes unnoticed or is forgotten. What can you do today to honor their presence and ensure they are not overlooked like the men of Nasa fled?
?
The correct relative adjective for Nasa is 'Nasai' or 'Nasawi'. How often do you pay attention to the proper names and titles of others? What does getting someone's name right say about your respect for them? Commit to learning and using the correct names of people you encounter this week.

Life of Imam al-Taftazani
intermediate
5 min
Al-Taftazani's Early Education and Move to Samarkand
Account of al-Taftazani's unknown early studies and his sudden appearance in Samarkand's scholarly circles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the gaps in al-Taftazani's early biography and his immersion in philosophical debates in Samarkand.

Core Idea
History sometimes leaves blank pages, but the few clues show a brilliant mind.

We know little about al-Taftazani's first years of study. However, by the time he appears in Samarkand, he is part of advanced debates on Aristotle and Ibn Sina. This lesson examines what we do know and the scholarly environment he entered.

Guided Path
1
Read paragraphs 2 and 3
Read about al-Taftazani's early education in Nasa and his sudden move to Samarkand.
The text admits ignorance about his early years.
2
Note the unknown details
The author states we do not know how many years he spent in Nasa nor the details of his early learning. Appreciate the historical silence.
3
Understand the Samarkand scene
In Samarkand, he engaged with advanced students debating Aristotle, Ibn Sina, al-Farabi, and criticizing Plato. This shows his high level.
The mention of 'curses on Plato' indicates a rejection of Neoplatonic emanationism.
4
Reflect on the significance
This passage shows that al-Taftazani was already a master of philosophy and kalam by the time he reached Samarkand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشأته
ولد التفتازاني بقرية تفتازان التابعة لمدينة (نسا) وهي مدينة بخراسان . تحيط بها سرخس ومرو ونیسابور، ويعلل العلماء سبب تسميتها بهذا الاسم أن المسلمين لما وردوا خراسان قصدوها فبلغ أهلها أخبار الجيش المغير الفاتح فهربوا، ولم يتخلف بها غير النساء، فلما أتاها المسلمون لم يجدوا فيها رجلاً واحداً فقالوا: هؤلاء نساء والنساء لا يقاتلن فننسى أمرها الآن إلى أن يعود رجالهن فتركوها ومضوا فسميت بذلك (نسا) والنسبة الصحيحة إليها (نسائي) وقيل نسوي أيضاً.
وهذه المدينة كانت ملتقى أبناء المسلمين النازحين إليها لحفظ القرآن والتفقه في أمور الدين، ولقد ترك التفتازاني قريته الصغيرة ورحل إلى (نسا) ولا ندري كم من الأعوام قضاها في تلك المدينة؟ ولا الحلقات الأولى التي تلقى فيها قواعد الخط وإملاء الكتابة واستظهار القرآن والتفقه في أمور الدين؟
لا شك أنه عاش فيها فترة يهملها التاريخ تماماً حتى يحدثنا ابن العماد الحنبلي بأنه يترك (نسا) وينتقل فجأة إلى سمرقند ويظهر ظهوراً بارعاً في حلقة طلاب كبار ودعوا عهد الطفولة وأخذوا يعبون من المعرفة عباً، ويصاولون أستاذهم في أقيسة أرسطو وشذرات ابن سينا وتهويمات الفارابي في مدينته الفاضلة ويصبون اللعنات على أفلاطون لقوله بنظرية العقول العشرة.
كم بقي التفتازاني في سمرقند؟ إننا لا نكاد نعلم شيئاً عن الفترة الأولى التي قضاها في سمرقند حتى إذا كان عام ٧٤٢هـ ينتقل فجأة إلى جرجانية وهي مدينة عظيمة على شاطىء نهر جيحون وأهل خوارزم يسمونها بلسانهم كر كانج فعربت إلى الجرجانية. يصفها صاحب معجم البلدان بأنها أعظم المدن التي رآها وأكثرها أموالاً وأحسنها أحوالاً.
دخل التفتازاني هذه المدينة وهو عالم كبير تسبقه شهرته لشرحه کتاب التصريف للزنجاني ولقد أعجبه المقام في هذه المدينة وعكف على التأليف والتصنيف وأصبح له طلاب وتلاميذ يتسابقون إليه ويجنون الثمار من بين يديه وفيها أتم كتابه (المطول على التلخيص).
ما كاد يهل عام ٧٤٨هـ حتى قرر الرحيل من الجرجانية إلى بلدة (هراة) وهي مدينة عظيمة مشهورة من أمهات مدن خراسان فيها بساتين كثيرة ومياه غزيرة وخيرات وفيرة حتى قال شاعرها أحمد السامي الهروي:
هراة أرض خصبها واسع ونبتها اللقاح والنرجس ما أحد منها إلى غيرها يخرج إلا بعد ما يفلس
ويقول الأديب البارع الزوزني:
هراة أردت مقامي بها لشتى فضائلها الوافرة الشمال وأعنابها وأعين غزلانها الساحرة
وكانت (هراة) في ذلك مملوءة بالعلماء وبأهل الفضل والحكمة ومساجدها تضج بالمناقشات العلمية وصولات العلماء ومختلف الآراء والأفكار ومن علماء (هراة) الحسين بن إدريس الهروي المحدث روى عنه ابن حبان. وللحسين هذا كتاب في التاريخ صنفه على حروف المعجم.
إلى هذه المدينة التي تموج بكل أنواع الحياة ألقى السعد رحله فيها وكان يتأبط كتابه الضخم المطول على التلخيص والذي كتبه في جرجانية فأهداه إلى ملك (هراة) معز الدين أبو الحسين بمجرد دخوله إلى المدينة.
His upbringing
Al-Taftazani was born in the village of Taftazan, belonging to the city of Nasa, which is a city in Khurasan. Surrounding it are Sarakhs, Marw, and Nishapur. Scholars explain the reason for its naming by this name: that when the Muslims came to Khurasan, they headed toward it, and its inhabitants learned of the news of the conquering army, so they fled, and none remained in it but the women. When the Muslims arrived, they did not find a single man there, so they said: 'These are women, and women do not fight, so we will postpone its matter until their men return.' So they left it and went on, thus it was named Nasa. The correct relative adjective to it is Nasai, and it is also said Nasawi.
This city was a meeting place for the sons of Muslims who migrated to it for memorizing the Quran and gaining understanding in matters of religion. Al-Taftazani left his small village and traveled to Nasa, and we do not know how many years he spent in that city, nor the first circles in which he received the rules of handwriting, dictation of writing, memorization of the Quran, and understanding in matters of religion.
There is no doubt that he lived in it for a period that history completely neglects, until Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali tells us that he leaves Nasa and suddenly moves to Samarkand and appears brilliantly in the circle of older students who have left childhood behind and drink deeply of knowledge, and they wrestle with their teacher in Aristotle's syllogisms, Ibn Sina's fragments, al-Farabi's fantasies in his Virtuous City, and they heap curses on Plato for his theory of the ten intellects.
How long did al-Taftazani remain in Samarkand? We hardly know anything about the first period he spent in Samarkand until the year 742 AH, when he suddenly moves to Jurjaniyya, which is a great city on the bank of the Jayhun River. The people of Khwarazm call it in their language 'Kar Kang', which was Arabized to al-Jurjaniyya. The author of Mu'jam al-Buldan describes it as the greatest city he had seen, the wealthiest in resources, and the best in conditions.
Al-Taftazani entered this city, a great scholar preceded by his reputation for his commentary on al-Zanjani's book al-Tasrif. He was pleased with staying in this city and devoted himself to authorship and composition. He acquired students and disciples who raced to him and harvested the fruits from his hands. In it he completed his book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis.
Hardly had the year 748 AH begun when he decided to travel from Jurjaniyya to the town of Herat, a great and famous city, one of the mother cities of Khurasan. It has many gardens, abundant waters, and plentiful bounties, so much so that its poet Ahmad al-Sami al-Harawi said:
Herat is a land whose fertility is vast, its plants are the pollen and the narcissus. No one leaves it for another except after going bankrupt.
And the accomplished adib al-Zawzani says:
Herat, I desired my stay in it for the sake of various abundant virtues: the north wind, its grapes, and the captivating eyes of its gazelles.
And Herat at that time was filled with scholars, people of virtue and wisdom. Its mosques teemed with scientific discussions and the assaults of scholars and various opinions and ideas. Among the scholars of Herat was al-Husayn ibn Idris al-Harawi, the hadith scholar, from whom Ibn Hibban narrated. This al-Husayn has a book on history arranged alphabetically.
To this city, teeming with all kinds of life, al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) cast his saddle, carrying his great book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis, which he had written in Jurjaniyya, and he presented it to the king of Herat, Mu'izz al-Din Abu al-Husayn, as soon as he entered the city.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative detailing the early life and scholarly travels of al-Taftazani, the author of Sharh al-Maqasid. It begins by noting his birthplace in the village of Taftazan, part of the city of Nasa in Khurasan. The author provides an anecdote about the naming of Nasa: when Muslims first arrived, the men fled, leaving only women, so the name Nasa was derived from 'nisa' (women). He then notes the correct nisba (relative adjective) is 'Nasai' or 'Nasawi'.
The passage explains that Nasa was a center for Quran memorization and religious learning, and al-Taftazani left his village to study there. The details of his early education are unknown. He then moved to Samarkand, where he joined advanced students engaging in debates on Aristotelian logic, Ibn Sina's philosophy, and al-Farabi's ideas, as well as criticizing Plato's theory of ten intellects.
The narrative continues with his move to Jurjaniyya in 742 AH, a city on the Jayhun River with great wealth. He was already renowned for his commentary on al-Zanjani's al-Tasrif. In Jurjaniyya, he devoted himself to writing and teaching, completing his major work al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis.
In 748 AH, he relocated to Herat, praised poetically for its fertility and beauty. Herat was a center of learning, with scholars like al-Husayn ibn Idris al-Harawi. Al-Taftazani presented his al-Mutawwal to the ruler Mu'izz al-Din Abu al-Husayn upon arrival. The passage thus covers his geographical and intellectual journey, highlighting his growing reputation and scholarly output.

أرسطو
ابن سينا
الفارابي
أفلاطون

B) They ignored him

D) They debated him

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's early life is obscure, but his emergence in Samarkand shows a mastery of philosophy and kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage reveals that al-Taftazani’s early years are almost completely unknown—history neglects the period when he memorized the Quran and learned the basics. Reflect: Are you comfortable working on your faith and knowledge when no one is watching and no record is kept? How does this silence challenge your need for recognition?
?
Imagine the unseen efforts that must have filled the gap between al-Taftazani’s departure from Nasa and his sudden brilliant appearance in Samarkand. What hidden preparation are you neglecting right now that, if consistent, could bring you to a similar turning point in your own life?
?
When you read that the Samarkand students ‘heap curses’ on Plato, do you feel the intensity of their conviction? What wrong belief or comfortable assumption in your own life have you been merely tolerating instead of actively refuting? Will you now seek to uproot it with the same passion?

Scholarly Maturity: Jurjaniyya and Herat
Al-Taftazani's major scholarly productions in Jurjaniyya and his final move to Herat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani's reputation grew through his commentary on al-Tasrif and his completion of al-Mutawwal, and his reception in Herat.

Core Idea
A scholar's journey is marked by cities where he leaves his intellectual legacy.

Al-Taftazani's travels continue as he moves to Jurjaniyya, where he completes his famous work al-Mutawwal. He then settles in Herat, a city teeming with scholars, and presents his book to the ruler. This lesson traces his scholarly maturity.

Guided Path
1
Read paragraphs 4-7
Read about the moves to Jurjaniyya and Herat, and the works produced.
2
Understand Jurjaniyya period
In Jurjaniyya, he completed al-Mutawwal and attracted students. His reputation preceded him due to his commentary on al-Tasrif.
Al-Tasrif is a work on morphology by al-Zanjani.
3

Herat is described poetically as fertile and beautiful, and as a center of learning with many scholars.
The poetry emphasizes the reluctance to leave Herat.
4

His upbringing
Al-Taftazani was born in the village of Taftazan, belonging to the city of Nasa, which is a city in Khurasan. Surrounding it are Sarakhs, Marw, and Nishapur. Scholars explain the reason for its naming by this name: that when the Muslims came to Khurasan, they headed toward it, and its inhabitants learned of the news of the conquering army, so they fled, and none remained in it but the women. When the Muslims arrived, they did not find a single man there, so they said: 'These are women, and women do not fight, so we will postpone its matter until their men return.' So they left it and went on, thus it was named Nasa. The correct relative adjective to it is Nasai, and it is also said Nasawi.
This city was a meeting place for the sons of Muslims who migrated to it for memorizing the Quran and gaining understanding in matters of religion. Al-Taftazani left his small village and traveled to Nasa, and we do not know how many years he spent in that city, nor the first circles in which he received the rules of handwriting, dictation of writing, memorization of the Quran, and understanding in matters of religion.
There is no doubt that he lived in it for a period that history completely neglects, until Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali tells us that he leaves Nasa and suddenly moves to Samarkand and appears brilliantly in the circle of older students who have left childhood behind and drink deeply of knowledge, and they wrestle with their teacher in Aristotle's syllogisms, Ibn Sina's fragments, al-Farabi's fantasies in his Virtuous City, and they heap curses on Plato for his theory of the ten intellects.

We hardly know anything about the first period he spent in Samarkand until the year 742 AH, when he suddenly moves to Jurjaniyya, which is a great city on the bank of the Jayhun River. The people of Khwarazm call it in their language 'Kar Kang', which was Arabized to al-Jurjaniyya. The author of Mu'jam al-Buldan describes it as the greatest city he had seen, the wealthiest in resources, and the best in conditions.
Al-Taftazani entered this city, a great scholar preceded by his reputation for his commentary on al-Zanjani's book al-Tasrif. He was pleased with staying in this city and devoted himself to authorship and composition. He acquired students and disciples who raced to him and harvested the fruits from his hands. In it he completed his book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis.

Herat is a land whose fertility is vast, its plants are the pollen and the narcissus. No one leaves it for another except after going bankrupt.

Herat, I desired my stay in it for the sake of various abundant virtues: the north wind, its grapes, and the captivating eyes of its gazelles.

In 748 AH, he relocated to Herat, praised poetically for its fertility and beauty. Herat was a center of learning, with scholars like al-Husayn ibn Idris al-Harawi. Al-Taftazani presented his al-Mutawwal to the ruler Mu'izz al-Din Abu al-Husayn upon arrival. The passage thus covers his geographical and intellectual journey, highlighting his growing reputation and scholarly output.

Al-Taftazani's scholarly peak came in Jurjaniyya with al-Mutawwal, and he gained recognition in Herat by presenting it to the ruler.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before al-Taftazani arrived in Jurjaniyya, his reputation preceded him because of his commentary on al-Tasrif. What reputation — what specific knowledge or character — is preceding you in your circles? Are you building something that will speak for you before you enter new doors?
?
Al-Taftazani left the wealth and comfort of Jurjaniyya for Herat, despite his success there. What comfort or success are you clinging to that may be keeping you from a place where you could bear more fruit for Allah? What would it cost you to leave it?
?
When al-Taftazani entered Herat, his first act was to present his greatest work to its ruler. If you were to present your 'book' — the sum of your learning and action — to your community or to Allah today, would it be a gift worthy of a ruler? What is missing from it that you must add before you meet your King?

Life of Imam al-Taftazani
beginner

Al-Taftazani's Travels and Scholarly Career
Biographical narrative describing al-Taftazani's journeys and scholarly works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key stages of al-Taftazani's travels and the major works he produced at each location.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's scholarly career was shaped by his extensive travels across Central Asia.

This passage traces the remarkable journey of one of the most influential scholars of the Islamic tradition. Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani was not only a prolific writer but also a traveler who moved from city to city, leaving a trail of important works. Understanding his movements helps us appreciate the intellectual environment in which he wrote his famous commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key cities Taftazani visited
As you read the passage, list the cities in order: Jurjaniya, Herat, Ham, Ghajdawan, Gulistan, Jurjaniya again, Sarakhs, Samarkand.
Pay attention to the dates given for each move.
2
Note the works completed in each city
For each city, find the title of the book Taftazani finished there, such as al-Mutawwal in Jurjaniya, Sharh al-Shamsiyya in Ham, etc.
The works are mentioned in passing; look for phrases like 'أتم فيها كتابه'.
3
Observe the pattern of movement
Notice that Taftazani often stayed only a few years in one place, except for the productive ten-year stay in Jurjaniya. Ask yourself why he moved so often.
Consider political and personal factors hinted at in the text.
4
Reflect on the Timurid connection
The passage ends with Timur summoning Taftazani. Consider how political events influenced scholarly careers.
This shows the interplay between rulers and scholars in medieval Islamic history.

فأرسل إليه يدعوه ثانية، فانتقل أخيه
Ten? How long did al-Taftazani remain in Samarkand? We hardly know anything about the first period he spent in Samarkand, until in the year 742 AH he suddenly moved to Jurjaniya, which is a great city on the bank of the Jayhun River. The people of Khwarazm call it in their language 'Kar Kangi', and it was Arabized to al-Jurjaniya. The author of Mu'jam al-Buldan describes it as the greatest city he had seen, the richest in wealth, and the best in conditions. Al-Taftazani entered this city as a great scholar whose fame preceded him, due to his commentary on Kitab al-Tasrif by al-Zanjani. He was pleased with staying in this city, devoted himself to authorship and composition, and acquired students and disciples who raced to him and reaped the fruits from his hands. In it he completed his book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis. The year 748 AH had hardly begun when he decided to travel from Jurjaniya to the town of Herat, which is a great and famous city, one of the mother cities of Khurasan, with many gardens, abundant waters, and plentiful bounties, until its poet Ahmad al-Sami al-Harawi said: 'Herat, its land is spacious in fertility, its plants are the pollen and the narcissus; no one leaves it for another except after going bankrupt.' And the excellent literary figure al-Zawzani says: 'I desired Herat as my abode for various abundant virtues: its breeze, its vineyards, and the enchanting eyes of its gazelles.' And Herat in that time was full of scholars and people of virtue and wisdom, and its mosques teemed with scientific discussions and scholars' contests, and various opinions and ideas. Among the scholars of Herat was al-Husayn ibn Idris al-Harawi, the hadith scholar, from whom Ibn Hibban narrated. And al-Husayn has a book on history which he arranged alphabetically. To this city, teeming with all kinds of life, Sa'd cast his burden, and he carried under his arm his great book al-Mutawwal 'ala al-Talkhis, which he wrote in Jurjaniya, and he presented it to the king of Herat, Mu'izz al-Din Abu al-Husayn, as soon as he entered the city. 79 (Do you think?) Do you think al-Taftazani's soul was satisfied and his spirit calmed by his stay near the gardens fragrant with perfume and the gardens filled with aroma? Most likely he was not at peace of mind nor tranquil in thought, because we did not find any notable production for him in this city. Or was he at peace of mind and tranquil in thought, and the bliss of life and comfortable living enticed laziness and led to relaxation? Four complete years he spent in Herat: how was he occupying his time? And in what works was he striking his thought? We are surprised to find him leaving Herat without a reason to leave, and migration, where he speeds to the town of Ham. And he found staying there pleasant, and his abode settled there, and he completed in it his book Sharh al-Shamsiyya on logic in the year 752 AH, then he left it for elsewhere. So when did he leave the town of Ham, and to which lands was his destination? We cannot determine a fixed date for his departure from this town. But Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali in his book Shadharat al-Dhahab tells us about his sudden presence in the year 756 AH in Ghajdawan, which is a village of Bukhara. And there he completed his book al-Mukhtasar 'ala al-Talkhis. And he did not find staying in the town of Ghajdawan pleasant for more than two years; after that he moved to Gulistan, one of the cities of Turkistan. And there he completed his book al-Talwih 'ala Tawdih Ghawamid al-Tanqih. And he remained in Gulistan for one year, then he returned from there to Herat in the year 759 AH, where he began composing his book Fatawa al-Hanafiyya. Then he left Herat for Jurjaniya, where he found his stay pleasant and settled there for about ten years. In fact, these ten were the most fruitful years of his life, during which he wrote Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya in the year 768 AH, and finished al-Irshad on grammar in the year 774 AH as mentioned by al-Shawkani, Ibn al-Imad, and al-Kanawi, or in the year 778 AH as mentioned by Tashkoprizadeh. And Khwandamir narrates that when Timur conquered Khwarazm, perhaps between the years 780 AH and 781 AH (1379 CE), King Muhammad al-Sarkhi ibn King Mu'izz al-Din Husayn Kart requested from ibn Pir Muhammad Ghiyath al-Din Pir Ali, who was at that time one of Timur's retinue, to ask his master's permission to send al-Taftazani to Sarakhs. Timur permitted, but he later recognized his virtue in knowledge, so he sent to summon him to Samarkand. Al-Taftazani initially hesitated to answer his invitation, excusing himself that he was preparing for travel to the Hijaz, so he sent to him a second invitation, and he moved to his brother.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative detailing the travels and scholarly career of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, the famous 14th-century scholar of kalam and Arabic sciences. The passage begins by noting the lack of information about Taftazani's early years in Samarkand until his sudden move to Jurjaniya in 742 AH. Jurjaniya, a great city on the Oxus, is described as wealthy and impressive, where Taftazani's fame preceded him. There he taught, wrote, and completed his commentary al-Mutawwal on al-Talkhis. In 748 AH he moved to Herat, a thriving intellectual center with many gardens and scholars. Despite the pleasant environment, Taftazani produced little during his four years there, leading to speculation about his inactivity. He then moved to Ham, where he completed Sharh al-Shamsiyya on logic in 752 AH. His movements become uncertain until he appears in Ghajdawan in 756 AH, completing al-Mukhtasar. He then spent two years there before moving to Gulistan, where he wrote al-Talwih. After a year, he returned to Herat to write Fatawa al-Hanafiyya, then back to Jurjaniya for ten productive years, during which he wrote his famous Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya (768 AH) and al-Irshad on grammar (774 AH). The narrative concludes with Timur's conquest of Khwarazm, after which Taftazani was invited to the court, initially hesitating but eventually moving to Sarakhs and then Samarkand at Timur's request.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Taftazani was a sedentary scholar who wrote all his works in one place.
Correction: In reality, his major works were composed in different cities across Central Asia, reflecting his extensive travels and diverse intellectual influences.

Checkpoint
In which city did al-Taftazani complete his work Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya?
A) Samarkand
B) Herat
C) Jurjaniya
D) Ghajdawan

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's scholarly legacy is intimately tied to his travels across Central Asia, where he produced some of the most influential works in Islamic theology and logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Taftazani's most productive season came after years of wandering and apparent inactivity. Where in your life do you feel you are 'wandering' right now, and how might God be preparing you for a future harvest? Are you willing to wait for that season, or are you anxious to produce now?
?
The author speculates that the comfort and beauty of Herat may have led al-Taftazani into laziness. Look at your own life: is there a 'Herat'—a comfortable situation—that is actually stifling your spiritual growth? What step will you take today to leave that comfort for fruitful toil?
?
Al-Taftazani's fame preceded him, and he gained students quickly in Jurjaniya. What reputation do you carry into new circles? Are you more concerned with building a name that impresses people, or with building substance that serves God?

Al-Taftazani's Restlessness in Herat and Journey to Ham
Describes al-Taftazani's restless stay in Herat and his move to Ham where he completed Sharh al-Shamsiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's early scholarly instability and his completion of his first major work, Sharh al-Shamsiyya, in Ham.

Core Idea
Travel and restlessness were early companions of al-Taftazani's scholarship.

The passage opens with a rhetorical question about al-Taftazani's contentment in Herat, noting his lack of output there. It then traces his journey to Ham, where he finally settled long enough to complete his first major work on logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the rhetorical questions and the contrast between Herat and Ham.
Notice the author's use of questions to engage the reader.
2
Identify the key locations
Identify Herat and Ham. What was al-Taftazani doing in each place?
3
Note the date of Sharh al-Shamsiyya
The passage explicitly states the year 752 AH for the completion of Sharh al-Shamsiyya. This is important for his biography.
This is one of his earliest works.
4
Reflect on productivity
Consider the contrast between his unproductive years in Herat and the completion of a major work in Ham. What might explain this?
The passage suggests that ease may lead to laziness.

Do you think al-Taftazani was pleased and his soul calmed by his stay near the fragrant gardens and flower-filled meadows? Most likely he was not at ease, nor at rest of mind, because we did not find any notable production from him in this city, or was he at ease and rest of mind, and the pleasures of life and abundance tempt laziness and push to laxity? He spent four complete years in Herat; how did he occupy his time? And in what works did he exert his thought? We are surprised that he leaves Herat without any reason to depart or emigrate, hastening to the town of Ham. There he was pleased to stay and settled, and there he completed his book (Sharh al-Shamsiyya) on logic in the year 752 AH, then he left it for elsewhere. When did he leave Ham and to which land did he head? We cannot fix a definite date for his departure from this town. But Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali in his book (Shadharat al-Dhahab) tells us of his sudden presence in 756 AH in Ghijduwan, which is a village of Bukhara. There he completed his book (al-Mukhtasar 'ala al-Talkhis). He did not stay in Ghijduwan more than two years, after which he moved to Kaltastan, one of the cities of Turkestan. There he completed his book (al-Talwih 'ala Tawdih Ghawamid al-Tanqih). He remained in Kaltastan for one year, then returned again to Herat in 759 AH, where he began composing his book (Fatawa al-Hanafiyya). Then he left Herat for Jurjaniyya, where he was pleased to stay and settled for about ten years. Indeed these ten were the most fruitful years of his life, for he wrote (Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya) in 768 AH, and completed (al-Irshad) on grammar in 774 AH as mentioned by al-Shawkani, Ibn al-Imad, and al-Kanawi, or in 778 AH as mentioned by Tashkubri Zada. It is related by Khwandamir that when Timur conquered Khwarazm, likely between 780-781 AH (1379 CE), King Muhammad al-Surkhi ibn King Mu'izz al-Din Husayn Kart requested from Ibn Pir Muhammad Ghiyath al-Din Pir Ali, who was then among Timur's entourage, to ask his master to send al-Taftazani to Sarakhs. Timur granted permission, but later recognized his scholarly merit, so he sent to summon him to Samarkand. At first, al-Taftazani hesitated to respond to his invitation, excusing himself by preparing for travel to the Hijaz. So Timur sent to him a second invitation, and he moved - his brother? - to Samarkand, and Timur honored his arrival. In Samarkand, he wrote his great book (al-Maqasid) in 784 AH corresponding to 1383 CE. Then he left Samarkand for Sarakhs and undertook teaching there in 785 AH, and began composing his book (Talkhis al-Jami'). His stay in Sarakhs was not long, nor was he settled there, but he quickly returned to Samarkand, where the sweet river water is, and the channels that flow with water, and the gardens that cover the city's buildings; no house is without a garden and springs. He returned to the land of knowledge and scholars, where study circles and schools of learning, and forums of culture and knowledge. He returned to participate in scholarly debate and the wisdom of the sages, so that they might finally reach the best opinion and the profound wisdom that illuminates for them and for generations after them the paths of knowledge and fields of intellect. In Samarkand he completed his book (Tahdhib al-Mantiq) and the explanation of the third part of al-Miftah. In 789, he began writing his supercommentary on al-Kashshaf and completed it in the same year. Then what? Samarkand was the final destination that closed the curtain with a dark night on the life of this giant, where the book reached its end. But how was his death? And what do scholars decide regarding the end of this giant? That has a story.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing the travels and scholarly output of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. It begins by questioning whether al-Taftazani was content in Herat, noting that he produced little there. It then details his movements: he left Herat for Ham, where he completed Sharh al-Shamsiyya on logic in 752 AH. After leaving Ham, he appears suddenly in Ghijduwan in 756 AH, finishing al-Mukhtasar 'ala al-Talkhis. After two years he moved to Kaltastan, completing al-Talwih, then returned to Herat in 759 AH to begin Fatawa al-Hanafiyya. Subsequently he moved to Jurjaniyya, where he spent ten productive years writing Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya in 768 AH and al-Irshad in 774 or 778 AH. The passage then recounts his summons by Timur to Samarkand, initially hesitant due to plans for Hajj, but eventually he went, and in Samarkand he wrote his great work al-Maqasid in 784 AH. After a brief stay in Sarakhs for teaching, he returned to Samarkand, where he completed Tahdhib al-Mantiq and a commentary on the third part of al-Miftah, and in 789 AH he wrote a supercommentary on al-Kashshaf. The passage ends with a rhetorical note that Samarkand was his final destination and hints at a story about his death.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's early scholarly journey was marked by instability, but he still produced his first major work in Ham in 752 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that al-Taftazani spent four years in comfort producing nothing notable. Look at your own life: where have you been comfortable yet stagnant? What are you going to leave behind to become productive again?
?
Al-Taftazani moved without apparent reason to Ham and there wrote his first major work. What is the 'Ham' in your own journey that you are avoiding because you feel settled? What is one step you can take today to move toward it?

Life of Imam al-Taftazani
beginner

From Ghijduwan to Kaltastan and Back to Herat
Narrates al-Taftazani's travels from Ghijduwan to Kaltastan and back to Herat, listing works completed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's itinerant period between Ghijduwan, Kaltastan, and his return to Herat, including the works he completed in each location.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's scholarship was produced on the move, never staying long in one place.

The passage continues al-Taftazani's biography after his stay in Ham. It narrates his sudden appearance in Ghijduwan in 756 AH, his completion of al-Mukhtasar, his move to Kaltastan where he wrote al-Talwih, and his return to Herat in 759 AH to begin Fatawa al-Hanafiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the pattern: arrival, completion of a work, then departure.
The author uses a fast-paced narrative to reflect al-Taftazani's mobility.
2
List the three locations
Identify Ghijduwan, Kaltastan, and Herat. Note the dates and works associated with each.
3
Understand the time frame
This covers from 756 AH to 759 AH, just three years but multiple moves.
Contrast with the earlier four years in Herat.

فهل ترى التفتازاني طابت نفسه وهدأت روحه بمقامه بالقرب من البساتين الفواحة بالعطر، والحدائق المليئة بالأرج؟ غالب الظن أنه لم يكن هادىء البال، ولا مستريح الفكر، لأننا لم نجد له إنتاجاً يذكر في هذه المدينة، أم إنه كان هادىء البال ومستريح الفكر ونعيم الحياة، ورغد العيش يغريان بالكسل ويدفعان إلى التراخي ..؟ أربع سنوات كوامل قضاها في (هراة) كيف كان يشغل وقته؟ وفي أي الأعمال كان يقدح فكره؟ إننا نفاجأ به يغادر هراة من غير دعته إلى المغادرة، والهجرة، حيث يسرع السير إلى بلدة (حام) ولقد طاب له فيها المقام واستقر بها النوى ويفرغ فيها من كتابه (شرح الشمسية) في المنطق عام ٧٥٢هـ ثم يتركها إلى غيرها. فمتى ترك بلدة (حام) وإلى أي البلاد كانت وجهته؟ لا نستطيع أن نحدد تاريخاً ثابتاً لمفارقته لهذه البلدة. ولكن ابن العماد الحنبلي في كتابه (شذرات الذهب) يحدثنا عن وجوده فجأة عام ٧٥٦هـ . في (غجدوان) وهي من قرى بخارى ولقد أتم فيها كتابه (المختصر على التلخيص) ولا يطيب له المقام في بلدة (غجدوان) أكثر من عامين ينتقل بعدها إلى (كلتستان) إحدى مدن تركستان) وفيها يفرغ من كتابه التلويح على توضيح غوامض التنقيح) ويبقى في (كلتستان) عاماً واحداً ليعود منها مرة أخرى إلى ( هراة) عام ٧٥٩ هـ حيث يشرع في تأليف كتابه (فتاوى الحنفية) ثم يترك (مراة) إلى جرجانية حيث يطيب مقامه فيها فيستقر حوالي عشر سنوات، وفي الحقيقة كانت هذه العشر أخصب سني حياته، حيث كتب (شرح العقائد النسفية) سنة ٧٦٨ هـ . وفرغ من الإرشاد في النحو سنة ٧٧٤ هـ كما ذكره الشوكاني وابن العماد والكنوي أو سنة ۷۷۸ هـ كما ذكره (طاشكبري زاده) ويروي (خواندمين) أنه لما غزا (تيمور) خوارزم ولعل ذلك بين عامي ٧٨٠هـ ٧٨١هـ ۱۳۷۹م طلب ملك محمد السرخي بن ملك معز الدين حسين كرت إلى ابن بير محمد غياث الدين بير علي. وكان يومئذ من بطانة تيمور أن يستأذن مولاه في إيفاد التفتازاني إلى سرخس، فأذن تيمور ولكنه عرف بعد ذلك فضله في العلم، فأرسل إليه يستقدمه إلى سمرقند وقعد التفتازاني أول الأمر عن إجابة دعوته، معتذراً بأنه يتهيأ للسفر إلى الحجاز فأرسل إليه يدعوه ثانية، فانتقل أخيه إلى سمرقند وأكرم تيمور وفادته وفي سمرقند ألف كتابه العظيم (المقاصد) عام ٧٨٤ هـ الموافق ۱۳۸۳ م . ثم غادر سمرقند إلى سرخس وتولى التدريس فيها عام ٧٨٥ هـ وشرع في تأليف كتابه (تلخيص بستان وعيون .، عاد لبلد العلم والعلماء حيث حلقات الدرس ومدارس العلم، وأنـديـة الثقافة والمعرفة عاد ليشارك في جدل العلماء، وعلم الحكماء ليصلوا في النهاية إلى الرأي الأمثل، والحكمة البالغة التي تنير لهم، ولمن يأتي بعدهم من أجيال وأجيال دروب المعرفة، وساحات العقول . وفي سمرقند أكمل كتابه (تهذيب المنطق) وشرح القسم الثالث من المفتاح . وفي عام ۷۸۹ شرع في كتابة حاشيته على الكشاف فأتمها في العام نفسه ثم ماذا؟ لقد كانت سمرقند هي نهاية المطاف التي أطبقت بليل دامس على حياة هذا العملاق حيث بلغ الكتاب أجله . ولكن كيف كانت وفاته . . ؟ وماذا يقرر العلماء في نهاية هذا العملاق . . ؟ إن لذلك قصة

Most likely he was not at ease, nor at rest of mind, because we did not find any notable production from him in this city, or was he at ease and rest of mind, and the pleasures of life and abundance tempt laziness and push to laxity? The Productive Decade in Jurjaniyya
Describes al-Taftazani's ten-year stay in Jurjaniyya and his most productive period, listing key works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Taftazani's most productive period was his ten-year stay in Jurjaniyya, during which he wrote his famous works Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya and al-Irshad.

Core Idea
The Jurjaniyya decade was the most fruitful of al-Taftazani's scholarly life.

Leaving Herat, al-Taftazani settled in Jurjaniyya for about ten years. The passage emphasizes that this was his most productive period, highlighting two major works: Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya on theology and al-Irshad on grammar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the emphasis on the ten-year stay being the most fruitful.
2
Identify the two major works
Find the names of the works: Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya (768 AH) and al-Irshad (774 or 778 AH). Understand what subjects they cover.
3
Note the conflicting dates
The passage gives two possible dates for al-Irshad, showing scholarly disagreement. This is common in biographical sources.

بستان وعيون .، عاد لبلد العلم والعلماء حيث حلقات الدرس ومدارس العلم، وأنـديـة الثقافة والمعرفة عاد ليشارك في جدل العلماء، وعلم الحكماء ليصلوا في النهاية إلى الرأي الأمثل، والحكمة البالغة التي تنير لهم، ولمن يأتي بعدهم من أجيال وأجيال دروب المعرفة، وساحات العقول . وفي سمرقند أكمل كتابه (تهذيب المنطق) وشرح القسم الثالث من المفتاح . وفي عام ۷۸۹ شرع في كتابة حاشيته على الكشاف فأتمها في العام نفسه ثم ماذا؟ لقد كانت سمرقند هي نهاية المطاف التي أطبقت بليل دامس على حياة هذا العملاق حيث بلغ الكتاب أجله . ولكن كيف كانت وفاته . . ؟ وماذا يقرر العلماء في نهاية هذا العملاق . . ؟ إن لذلك قصة
Do you think al-Taftazani was pleased and his soul calmed by his stay near the fragrant gardens and flower-filled meadows? Most likely he was not at ease, nor at rest of mind, because we did not find any notable production from him in this city, or was he at ease and rest of mind, and the pleasures of life and abundance tempt laziness and push to laxity? He spent four complete years in Herat; how did he occupy his time? And in what works did he exert his thought? We are surprised that he leaves Herat without any reason to depart or emigrate, hastening to the town of Ham. There he was pleased to stay and settled, and there he completed his book (Sharh al-Shamsiyya) on logic in the year 752 AH, then he left it for elsewhere. When did he leave Ham and to which land did he head? We cannot fix a definite date for his departure from this town. But Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali in his book (Shadharat al-Dhahab) tells us of his sudden presence in 756 AH in Ghijduwan, which is a village of Bukhara. There he completed his book (al-Mukhtasar 'ala al-Talkhis). He did not stay in Ghijduwan more than two years, after which he moved to Kaltastan, one of the cities of Turkestan. There he completed his book (al-Talwih 'ala Tawdih Ghawamid al-Tanqih). He remained in Kaltastan for one year, then returned again to Herat in 759 AH, where he began composing his book (Fatawa al-Hanafiyya). Then he left Herat for Jurjaniyya, where he was pleased to stay and settled for about ten years. Indeed these ten were the most fruitful years of his life, for he wrote (Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya) in 768 AH, and completed (al-Irshad) on grammar in 774 AH as mentioned by al-Shawkani, Ibn al-Imad, and al-Kanawi, or in 778 AH as mentioned by Tashkubri Zada. It is related by Khwandamir that when Timur conquered Khwarazm, likely between 780-781 AH (1379 CE), King Muhammad al-Surkhi ibn King Mu'izz al-Din Husayn Kart requested from Ibn Pir Muhammad Ghiyath al-Din Pir Ali, who was then among Timur's entourage, to ask his master to send al-Taftazani to Sarakhs. Timur granted permission, but later recognized his scholarly merit, so he sent to summon him to Samarkand. At first, al-Taftazani hesitated to respond to his invitation, excusing himself by preparing for travel to the Hijaz. So Timur sent to him a second invitation, and he moved - his brother? - to Samarkand, and Timur honored his arrival. In Samarkand, he wrote his great book (al-Maqasid) in 784 AH corresponding to 1383 CE. Then he left Samarkand for Sarakhs and undertook teaching there in 785 AH, and began composing his book (Talkhis al-Jami'). His stay in Sarakhs was not long, nor was he settled there, but he quickly returned to Samarkand, where the sweet river water is, and the channels that flow with water, and the gardens that cover the city's buildings; no house is without a garden and springs. He returned to the land of knowledge and scholars, where study circles and schools of learning, and forums of culture and knowledge. He returned to participate in scholarly debate and the wisdom of the sages, so that they might finally reach the best opinion and the profound wisdom that illuminates for them and for generations after them the paths of knowledge and fields of intellect. In Samarkand he completed his book (Tahdhib al-Mantiq) and the explanation of the third part of al-Miftah. In 789, he began writing his supercommentary on al-Kashshaf and completed it in the same year. Then what? Samarkand was the final destination that closed the curtain with a dark night on the life of this giant, where the book reached its end. But how was his death? And what do scholars decide regarding the end of this giant? That has a story.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing the travels and scholarly output of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. It begins by questioning whether al-Taftazani was content in Herat, noting that he produced little there. It then details his movements: he left Herat for Ham, where he completed Sharh al-Shamsiyya on logic in 752 AH. After leaving Ham, he appears suddenly in Ghijduwan in 756 AH, finishing al-Mukhtasar 'ala al-Talkhis. After two years he moved to Kaltastan, completing al-Talwih, then returned to Herat in 759 AH to begin Fatawa al-Hanafiyya. Subsequently he moved to Jurjaniyya, where he spent ten productive years writing Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya in 768 AH and al-Irshad in 774 or 778 AH. The passage then recounts his summons by Timur to Samarkand, initially hesitant due to plans for Hajj, but eventually he went, and in Samarkand he wrote his great work al-Maqasid in 784 AH. After a brief stay in Sarakhs for teaching, he returned to Samarkand, where he completed Tahdhib al-Mantiq and a commentary on the third part of al-Miftah, and in 789 AH he wrote a supercommentary on al-Kashshaf. The passage ends with a rhetorical note that Samarkand was his final destination and hints at a story about his death.

Key Terms
جرجانية
شرح العقائد النسفية
الإرشاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Taftazani's most productive years were in Samarkand.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the ten years in Jurjaniyya were the most fruitful, not Samarkand.

Checkpoint

C) 774 AH

Key Takeaway
The ten years in Jurjaniyya were al-Taftazani's most productive, culminating in Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya and al-Irshad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If al-Taftazani's most fruitful years were a concentrated decade of settled work, what is the single project or pursuit that you need to settle into right now to make your next ten years fruitful? What is preventing you from beginning it today?
?
The passage says these were 'the most fruitful years' of his life. What would it take for you to look back on the next ten years of your life and say the same? Are you willing to make the sacrifices needed to remove distractions and focus on what truly matters?
?
Al-Taftazani produced works that have shaped Islamic scholarship for centuries. What legacy will you leave with the time and knowledge Allah has given you? What do you need to start doing today to build that legacy?

The Invitation to Samarkand and Final Works
Narrates al-Taftazani's summons to Samarkand by Timur, his writing of al-Maqasid, and his final works and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's summons by Timur to Samarkand, his completion of al-Maqasid, and his final scholarly activities and death in Samarkand.

Core Idea
Samarkand was both the pinnacle of al-Taftazani's career and his final resting place.

The passage details how Timur, after initially allowing al-Taftazani to go to Sarakhs, recognized his merit and summoned him to Samarkand. There he wrote his magnum opus al-Maqasid, and later returned after a brief stint in Sarakhs to complete more works before his death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. This is a longer passage covering several years.
2
Understand the Timurid context
Note the political context: Timur's conquest of Khwarazm and his interaction with scholars.
3
Identify the key works written in Samarkand
List: al-Maqasid (784 AH), Tahdhib al-Mantiq, commentary on al-Miftah, and the supercommentary on al-Kashshaf (789 AH).
4
Reflect on the final years
The passage ends with a rhetorical note about his death, hinting at a story.

(خواندمين) أنه لما غزا (تيمور) خوارزم ولعل ذلك بين عامي ٧٨٠هـ ٧٨١هـ ۱۳۷۹م طلب ملك محمد السرخي بن ملك معز الدين حسين كرت إلى ابن بير محمد غياث الدين بير علي. وكان يومئذ من بطانة تيمور أن يستأذن مولاه Do you think al-Taftazani was pleased and his soul calmed by his stay near the fragrant gardens and flower-filled meadows? Most likely he was not at ease, nor at rest of mind, because we did not find any notable production from him in this city, or was he at ease and rest of mind, and the pleasures of life and abundance tempt laziness and push to laxity? He spent four complete years in Herat; how did he occupy his time? And in what works did he exert his thought? We are surprised that he leaves Herat without any reason to depart or emigrate, hastening to the town of Ham. There he was pleased to stay and settled, and there he completed his book (Sharh al-Shamsiyya) on logic in the year 752 AH, then he left it for elsewhere. When did he leave Ham and to which land did he head? We cannot fix a definite date for his departure from this town. But Ibn al-Imad al-Hanbali in his book (Shadharat al-Dhahab) tells us of his sudden presence in 756 AH in Ghijduwan, which is a village of Bukhara. There he completed his book (al-Mukhtasar 'ala al-Talkhis). He did not stay in Ghijduwan more than two years, after which he moved to Kaltastan, one of the cities of Turkestan. There he completed his book (al-Talwih 'ala Tawdih Ghawamid al-Tanqih). He remained in Kaltastan for one year, then returned again to Herat in 759 AH, where he began composing his book (Fatawa al-Hanafiyya). Then he left Herat for Jurjaniyya, where he was pleased to stay and settled for about ten years. Indeed these ten were the most fruitful years of his life, for he wrote (Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya) in 768 AH, and completed (al-Irshad) on grammar in 774 AH as mentioned by al-Shawkani, Ibn al-Imad, and al-Kanawi, or in 778 AH as mentioned by Tashkubri Zada. It is related by Khwandamir that when Timur conquered Khwarazm, likely between 780-781 AH (1379 CE), King Muhammad al-Surkhi ibn King Mu'izz al-Din Husayn Kart requested from Ibn Pir Muhammad Ghiyath al-Din Pir Ali, who was then among Timur's entourage, to ask his master to send al-Taftazani to Sarakhs. Timur granted permission, but later recognized his scholarly merit, so he sent to summon him to Samarkand. At first, al-Taftazani hesitated to respond to his invitation, excusing himself by preparing for travel to the Hijaz. So Timur sent to him a second invitation, and he moved - his brother? - to Samarkand, and Timur honored his arrival. In Samarkand, he wrote his great book (al-Maqasid) in 784 AH corresponding to 1383 CE. Then he left Samarkand for Sarakhs and undertook teaching there in 785 AH, and began composing his book (Talkhis al-Jami'). His stay in Sarakhs was not long, nor was he settled there, but he quickly returned to Samarkand, where the sweet river water is, and the channels that flow with water, and the gardens that cover the city's buildings; no house is without a garden and springs. He returned to the land of knowledge and scholars, where study circles and schools of learning, and forums of culture and knowledge. He returned to participate in scholarly debate and the wisdom of the sages, so that they might finally reach the best opinion and the profound wisdom that illuminates for them and for generations after them the paths of knowledge and fields of intellect. In Samarkand he completed his book (Tahdhib al-Mantiq) and the explanation of the third part of al-Miftah. In 789, he began writing his supercommentary on al-Kashshaf and completed it in the same year. Then what? Samarkand was the final destination that closed the curtain with a dark night on the life of this giant, where the book reached its end. But how was his death? And what do scholars decide regarding the end of this giant? That has a story.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing the travels and scholarly output of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. It begins by questioning whether al-Taftazani was content in Herat, noting that he produced little there. It then details his movements: he left Herat for Ham, where he completed Sharh al-Shamsiyya on logic in 752 AH. Al-Taftazani's Final Years in Samarkand
Biographical narrative of al-Taftazani's later life and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events and scholarly works of al-Taftazani's later life, as narrated in this biographical passage.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's late career peaked in Samarkand with major works.

This passage narrates the final chapter of al-Taftazani's life, focusing on his time in Samarkand under Timur's patronage. It highlights his major writings, his brief relocation to Sarakhs, and his eventual return to the intellectual hub of Samarkand, where he engaged with scholars and completed significant works. The passage also sets up the mystery surrounding his death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the poetic descriptions of Samarkand and the sequence of events.
The Arabic uses vivid imagery for Samarkand's gardens and canals.
2
Identify key events and works
List the events in order: arrival in Samarkand, writing al-Maqasid, move to Sarakhs, return, completion of Tahdhib al-Mantiq and the gloss on al-Kashshaf.
Note the dates given for each work.
3
Reflect on the death mystery
The passage ends by raising questions about his death. Consider why the author leaves this open-ended and what it suggests about the sources.
This prepares us for a later account.
