هنا تأتي الصعوبات أمام الباحث عندما يطلب أحد المراجع ويفاجأ من بأن يد الضياع قد طوته فيما طوت من مؤلفاته وكنوز . وهذا البحث الذي بين أيدينا يحتوي على آثار سعد الدين التفتازاني وقد قسم إلى قسمين : الأول : كتبه ومؤلفاته . الثاني : تلامذته وطلاب المعرفة في مدرسته.
١ - الأربعين في الحديث : علم الحديث هذا الكتاب ذكره صاحب كتاب كشف الظنون عن أسامي الكتب والفنون .
٢ - رسالة في الإكراه : وهذه ذكرها صاحب كشف الظنون عن أسامي الكتب والفنون ج ١ ص ٨٤٧.
٣ - تلخيصه للكشاف عن حقائق التنزيل : للعلامة أبي القاسم جار الله محمود بن عمر الزمخشري الخوارزمي ، المتوفى سنة ٥٣٨هـ ولخصه التفتازاني من حاشية الطيبي على الكشاف مع زيادة تعقيد في العبارة ولم يتمها وقال وصل فيها إلى سورة الفتح، وفرغ منها سنة ٧٨٩هـ ويقال : إنه بدأ في تأليفه بسمرقند في ربيع الثاني عام
Here come the difficulties before the researcher when he requests a reference and is surprised that the hand of loss has folded it among what it folded of his works and treasures. And this research which is in our hands contains the works of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and has been divided into two parts: The first: his books and works. The second: his students and seekers of knowledge in his school.
1 - Al-Arba'in fi al-Hadith: The science of hadith. This book was mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun 'an Asami al-Kutub wa al-Funun.
2 - Risalah fi al-Ikrah: This was mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun 'an Asami al-Kutub wa al-Funun, vol. 1 p. 847.
3 - Talkhisuhu li al-Kashshaf 'an Haqa'iq al-Tanzil: By the eminent scholar Abu al-Qasim Jar Allah Mahmud ibn 'Umar al-Zamakhshari al-Khwarizmi, died 538 AH. Al-Taftazani abridged it from the Hashiyah of al-Tibi on al-Kashshaf with increased complexity in expression and did not complete it, and he said he reached Surah al-Fath and finished it in the year 789 AH, and it is said that he began its composition in Samarqand in Rabi' al-Thani year
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical introduction. It begins by lamenting the difficulty of finding lost works, then states that this research contains the works of al-Taftazani and is divided into two sections: his books and his students. Then it lists three of his works: (1) Al-Arba'in fi al-Hadith, a hadith work mentioned in Kashf al-Zunun; (2) Risalah fi al-Ikrah, also mentioned in Kashf al-Zunun; (3) Talkhis al-Kashshaf, his abridgment of al-Zamakhshari's tafsir, which he based on al-Tibi's commentary but made more complex, and he only reached Surah al-Fath, completing it in 789 AH, and he began it in Samarqand in Rabi' al-Thani (year cut off). This listing serves to introduce the reader to some of al-Taftazani's key writings.

Key Terms

رسالة في الإكراه
تلخيص الكشاف
كشف الظنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Taftazani only wrote theological works.
Correction: This passage shows he also wrote on hadith, fiqh, and tafsir.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani authored works in multiple disciplines, including hadith, fiqh, and tafsir, as illustrated by these three titles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a reference to a lost work in a book you're studying, does it stir any urgency in you to preserve and pass on what you have? What steps will you take today to ensure your own knowledge is not lost?
?
Al-Taftazani labored over a complex abridgment and left it unfinished. Do you have any half-finished attempts at deepening your understanding of the deen? Will you intentionally revisit them, even if they seem difficult?
?
The passage mentions 'the hand of loss' folding away precious works. What currently occupies your time that might be forgotten forever if you don't act? How can you invest your energy in something that will outlast you?

Al-Taftazani's Authorial Legacy
Lists al-Taftazani's authored works with descriptions and references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the range of al-Taftazani's authored works across hadith, tafsir, and fiqh, and how later bibliographers preserved his scholarly output.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's works span hadith, tafsir, and fiqh, documented by later bibliographers.

This lesson presents a bibliographic listing of al-Taftazani's authored works. Rather than a continuous argument, the passage functions as a reference list, compiled from later sources such as Kashf al-Zunun. We will examine each entry to understand the scope of his scholarship and the methods used to preserve his legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the list
Read the entire Arabic passage and its translation. This is a list, so pay attention to each item and its description.
The works are grouped by subject: hadith, tafsir, fiqh.
2
Categorize the works
Identify each work and note its subject area. For example, 'al-Arba'in fi al-Hadith' is a hadith work. Which works belong to tafsir? Which to fiqh?
There are also works on inheritance and a Persian exegesis.
3
Notice the source references
Most entries reference 'Kashf al-Zunun' by Hajji Khalifa. This shows how later bibliographers preserved knowledge of older works.
Some entries also mention manuscript locations, indicating the works' survival.

الأربعين في الحديث : هذا الكتاب ذكره صاحب كتاب كشف الظنون عن أسامي الكتب والفنون. رسالة في الإكراه : وهذه ذكرها صاحب كشف الظنون. التفسير تلخيصه للكشاف عن حقائق التنزيل : للعلامة أبي القاسم جار الله محمود بن عمر الزمخشري الخوارزمي المتوفى سنة ٥٣٨هـ ولخصه التفتازاني من حاشية الطيبي على الكشاف مع زيادة تعقيد في العبارة ولم يتمها وقال وصل فيها إلى سورة الفتح وفرغ منها سنة ٧٨٩هـ ويقال إنه بدأ في تأليفه بسمرقند في ربيع الثاني عام ٧٨٩هـ وتشمل هذه التعليقات من سورة البقرة إلى سورة هود الآية ٥٨ ومن سورة الزمر إلى سورة الطلاق ومنه مخطوطات في برلين تحت رقم ٧٩٣ وفي المتحف البريطاني وفي مكتبة وزارة الهند وفي غيرها من دور الكتب. كشف الأسرار وعدة الأبرار : تفسير فارسي للشيخ العلامة سعد الدين وظهر أن نسخة مخطوطة منه موجودة في مكتبة يكي جامع انظر فهرس هذه المكتبة ص ٨٠ رقم ٤٣. الفقه الفتاوى الحنفية : أفتاها بهراة ذكرها صاحب كتاب كشف الظنون جـ ٢ ص ٢٢٢. شرحه على فرائض السجاوندي: وهو الإمام سراج الدين محمد بن محمود عبد الرشيد السجاوندي الحنفي ويقال لها الفرائض السراجية ذكره صاحب كشف الظنون جـ ٢ ص ١٢٤٨. المفتاح في فروع الفقه الشافعي : ذكره صاحب كتاب كشف الظنون جـ ٢ ص ١٧٦٩ وتقول عنه دائرة المعارف الإسلامية هو مخطوط ببرلين تحت رقم ٤٦٠٤. اختصار شرح تلخيص الجامع الكبير : وهو موجز لم يتمه لشرح مسعود بن محمد الفجداوني على مختصر الخلاطي لرسالة الشيباني في فروع الفقه الشافعي المعروفة بالجامع الكبير ويروي صاحب روضات الجنات أن التفتازاني بدأ في تأليفه بسرخس عام ٧٨٥هـ ومنه مخطوط في مكتبة يكي جامع رقم ٤٢٨ مكرر وطبعت في دلهي.
The Forty in Hadith: This book was mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun about the names of books and arts. A Treatise on Duress: And this was mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun. Exegesis: His abridgement of al-Kashshaf about the realities of revelation: by the scholar Abu al-Qasim Jar Allah Mahmud ibn Umar al-Zamakhshari al-Khwarizmi, died 538 AH; al-Taftazani abridged it from al-Tibi's gloss on al-Kashshaf with increased complexity in expression, and he did not complete it; he said he reached Surah al-Fath in it, and finished it in 789 AH, and it is said he began composing it in Samarqand in Rabi' al-Thani year 789 AH. These annotations cover from Surah al-Baqarah to Surah Hud verse 58, and from Surah al-Zumar to Surah al-Talaq. Manuscripts of it exist in Berlin under number 793, in the British Museum, in the library of the Indian Ministry, and in other libraries. Unveiling of Secrets and Provision of the Pious: A Persian exegesis by the scholar Sad al-Din, and it appears a manuscript copy exists in the Yeki Jami library; see the catalog of this library p. 80 no. 43. Jurisprudence: Hanafi Legal Opinions: He issued them (in Herat); mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun vol. 2 p. 222. His commentary on al-Sajawandi's Inheritance Rules: He is Imam Siraj al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud Abd al-Rashid al-Sajawandi al-Hanafi, and it is called al-Fara'id al-Sirajiyya; mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun vol. 2 p. 1248. The Key to Shafi'i Jurisprudence: Mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun vol. 2 p. 1769; the Encyclopedia of Islam says it is a manuscript in Berlin under number 4604. Abridgement of the Commentary on the Summary of al-Jami' al-Kabir: It is a summary, which he did not complete, of the commentary of Mas'ud ibn Muhammad al-Fajdawani on Mukhtasar al-Khilati of al-Shaybani's treatise on Shafi'i jurisprudence known as al-Jami' al-Kabir. The author of Rawdat al-Jinnat narrates that al-Taftazani began composing it in Sarakhs in 785 AH. A manuscript exists in the Yeki Jami library, number 428 repeated, and it was printed in Delhi.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic listing of the works of al-Taftazani, organized by subject area. It begins with his hadith works: al-Arba'in fi al-Hadith (The Forty in Hadith) and Risala fi al-Ikrah (A Treatise on Duress), both noted as referenced in Kashf al-Zunun. Under tafsir, it lists his abridgement of al-Zamakhshari's al-Kashshaf, which he adapted from al-Tibi's gloss. The description specifies the scope (Surahs covered) and the completion date (789 AH), and mentions manuscript locations. Next is Kashf al-Asrar wa 'Uddat al-Abrar, a Persian tafsir by Sad al-Din, with a manuscript noted. In fiqh, three works are listed: al-Fatawa al-Hanafiyya (Hanafi legal opinions issued in Herat), his commentary on al-Sajawandi's Fara'id (inheritance rules), al-Miftah fi Furu' al-Fiqh al-Shafi'i (Key to Shafi'i jurisprudence), and finally Ikhtisar Sharh Talkhis al-Jami' al-Kabir (an unfinished abridgement of a Shafi'i fiqh commentary). Each entry references Kashf al-Zunun as a source for the work's existence, and sometimes additional manuscript locations or details. The passage serves as a bibliography of al-Taftazani's authored works across multiple Islamic sciences, demonstrating his scholarly range and the later transmission of his writings.

Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi: Life and Works
Biography of the first disciple with education and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly biography of Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi, including his birth, education, travels, and his contributions to Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
A scholar's journey from prohibition to permission reveals the value of rational sciences.

This lesson introduces the first disciple of the author, Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi. His biography illustrates the traditional path of learning: initial resistance, later permission, study under great masters, travel, and patronage. It also highlights his two important works in logic, philosophy, and rhetoric.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the full name
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Pay attention to the vocalization of the name 'al-Abiwardi' as explained in the text.
The name is broken down with fatha, sukun, kasra, etc.
2
Identify birth year and place
Find the birth year (761 AH) and birthplace (Abiward in Khurasan). Understand the significance of his grandfather's migration.
3
Trace his educational journey
Follow his progression: initial prohibition by his father from rational sciences, then permission, his close study with al-Taftazani, travel to Baghdad, and study with al-Kurdi and al-Kirmani.
Notice the key teachers and locations.
4
Note his final destination and works
Read about his move to Yemen, appointment as teacher in Ta'izz, and his death in 816 AH. Then review the two works listed.
Works cover logic, philosophy, and balagha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلامذته وطلاب المعرفة في مدرسته
التلاميذ
۱ - حسام الدين بن علي بن محمد الأبيوردي بفتح الهمزة والواو، وسكون التحتية، وكسر الباء وسكون الراء .
ولد سنة إحدى وستين وسبعمائة بأبيورد بلدة بخراسان، المنتقل جده إليها ، ونشأ بها، وكان هو وأبوه يعرف كل منهما فيها بالخطيب ولذا قيل له الخطيبي(۱)
واشتغل بعلوم على جماعة من الكبار وكان أبوه يمنعه في الابتداء من الاشتغال بالعقليات ثم أذن له فسره ذلك ولازم السعد التفتازاني (٢) ملازمة جيدة ثم رحل إلى بغداد سنة ثلاثة وثمانين وسبعمائة وقرأ بها على الشهاب أحمد الكردي ، الحاوي في الفقه والغاية القصوى، ولازم فيها الشمس الكرماني .
ثم دخل اليمن واجتمع بالناصر ففوض إليه التدريس ببعض المدارس بتعز، فعاجلته المنية بها عام ٨١٦هـ .
من تصانيفه
۱ - حاشية على شرح مطالع الأنوار للأرموي في المنطق والحكمة (۳). ۲ - ربيع الجنان في المعاني والبيان (٤) .
(۱) راجع الضوء اللامع ج ۳ ص ۱۰۹ وما بعدها. (۲) المصدر السابق وشذرات الذهب ج ۷ ص ۱۲۰ . (۳) هدية العارفين ج ۱ ص ۲۷۸ . (٤) راجع كشف الظنون ج ۱ ص ۸۳۳ .
His disciples and seekers of knowledge at his school
Disciples
1 - Husam al-Din ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Abiwardi: with fatha on the hamza and waw, sukun on the ya', kasra on the ba', and sukun on the ra'.
He was born in the year 761 AH in Abiward, a town in Khurasan, to which his grandfather had moved, and he grew up there. He and his father were each known in it as al-Khatib, hence he was called al-Khatibi (1).
He studied various sciences with a group of senior scholars, and his father initially prevented him from engaging in the rational sciences, then permitted him, which delighted him. He closely attended al-Sa'd al-Taftazani (2) with excellent companionship. Then he traveled to Baghdad in the year 783 AH and studied there with al-Shihab Ahmad al-Kurdi, [author of] al-Hawi in fiqh and al-Ghaya al-Quswa, and he closely attended al-Shams al-Kirmani there.
Then he entered Yemen and met al-Nasir, who entrusted him with teaching at some schools in Ta'izz. Death overtook him there in the year 816 AH.
His works:
1 - Gloss on the commentary of Matali' al-Anwar by al-Urmawi on logic and philosophy (3). 2 - Rabi' al-Jinan in ma'ani and bayan (4).
(1) See: al-Daw' al-Lami', vol. 3, p. 109 ff. (2) Same source and Shadharat al-Dhahab, vol. 7, p. 120. (3) Hadiyyat al-'Arifin, vol. 1, p. 278. (4) See: Kashf al-Zunun, vol. 1, p. 833.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for the first disciple of the author. It begins with a heading 'Disciples' and lists Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi. It explains the vocalization of his name. It then gives his birth year (761 AH) and birthplace (Abiward in Khurasan), noting his grandfather's move there. He and his father were both known as al-Khatib. He studied with many senior scholars; his father initially forbade him from studying rational sciences but later permitted. He closely studied with al-Taftazani. He traveled to Baghdad in 783 AH and studied with al-Shihab Ahmad al-Kurdi and al-Shams al-Kirmani. Then he went to Yemen, met al-Nasir, who appointed him teacher in Ta'izz, where he died in 816 AH. The entry then lists two of his works: a gloss on the commentary of Matali' al-Anwar and Rabi' al-Jinan. Footnotes provide references to biographical sources. The passage follows a typical scholarly biography format: name, birth, education, teachers, travels, patronage, death, and works.

الأبيوردي
الخطيبي
السعد التفتازاني
حاشية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The father's initial prohibition of rational sciences implies that rational sciences were generally discouraged in that era.
Correction: The text states it was a personal pedagogical choice of his father, not a general prohibition. Later, the father permitted him, and al-Abiwardi became a scholar of rational sciences, as seen in his works.

Checkpoint
In which year did Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi die?
A) 761 AH
B) 783 AH
C) 816 AH
D) 826 AH

Key Takeaway
Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi was a scholar whose journey from initial prohibition to mastery of rational sciences and eventual teaching position in Yemen exemplifies the traditional scholarly path.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your father once prevented you from studying a subject that later became your passion. Was his prohibition a sign of lack of faith in you? Or was it a protective measure? And when permission finally came, did you embrace it with delight, or did resentment linger? Al-Abiwardi's delight upon permission is recorded. What would your reaction be?
?
You have studied with teachers, perhaps not as famous as al-Taftazani. But have you 'closely attended' any of them with 'excellent companionship'? The phrase 'لازم ملازمة جيدة' implies more than just attending classes. It means practical companionship, following, and serving. Whom do you accompany closely in seeking knowledge? And are you prepared to travel, as al-Abiwardi traveled to Baghdad and Yemen, to find the best teachers? If not, what is holding you back?
?
Al-Abiwardi authored works in logic, philosophy, and rhetoric—subjects that some might consider 'secular' or 'dangerous'. Yet he was given a teaching position in Ta'izz. Are there subjects you have avoided studying because of external discouragement? Could it be that your own hesitations mirror his father's initial prohibition? This lesson shows that permission led to a lifetime of contribution. Is there an area of knowledge you need to seek permission for—from yourself, from a mentor, or from Allah—and then dive into with delight? What step will you take today?

Biography of Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi
Biography of Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi, student of al-Taftazani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, teachers, and works of Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi, a prominent student of Sa‘d al-Taftazani.

Core Idea
A student's journey from prohibition to mastery through perseverance and travel.

This passage introduces the first student of al-Taftazani mentioned in the text: Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi. We learn about his name, birth, family background, his father's initial prohibition from rational sciences, his eventual permission, and his studies with numerous scholars including al-Taftazani. The biography also covers his travels, teaching positions, and his two known works.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: name explanation, birth, family, education, travels, death, works.
This is a standard format for Islamic biographical entries.
2
Identify key events
List the major events in al-Abiwardi's life: birth year, father's initial ban, association with Taftazani, travels to Baghdad and Yemen, teaching in Ta'izz, death.
3
Reflect on his scholarly journey
Consider the significance of his father's initial prohibition and later permission. How did this shape his career? Also note the scholars he studied with, especially al-Taftazani.
This highlights the importance of perseverance in seeking knowledge.
4
Examine his works
The passage lists two works. Understand their subjects: one is a gloss on logic and philosophy, the other on rhetoric. This shows his areas of expertise.
These works indicate his specialization in rational sciences and rhetoric.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱ - حسام الدين بن علي بن محمد الأبيوردي بفتح الهمزة والواو، وسكون التحتية، وكسر الباء وسكون الراء . ولد سنة إحدى وستين وسبعمائة بأبيورد بلدة بخراسان، المنتقل جده إليها ، ونشأ بها، وكان هو وأبوه يعرف كل منهما فيها بالخطيب ولذا قيل له الخطيبي واشتغل بعلوم على جماعة من الكبار وكان أبوه يمنعه في الابتداء من الاشتغال بالعقليات ثم أذن له فسره ذلك ولازم السعد التفتازاني ملازمة جيدة ثم رحل إلى بغداد سنة ثلاثة وثمانين وسبعمائة وقرأ بها على الشهاب أحمد الكردي ، الحاوي في الفقه والغاية القصوى، ولازم فيها الشمس الكرماني . ثم دخل اليمن واجتمع بالناصر ففوض إليه التدريس ببعض المدارس بتعز، فعاجلته المنية بها عام ۸۱۶هـ . من تصانيفه ۱ - حاشية على شرح مطالع الأنوار للأرموي في المنطق والحكمة . ۲ - ربيع الجنان في المعاني والبيان .
1 - Husam al-Din ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Abiwardi: with fatḥa on the hamza and waw, sukūn on the yāʾ, kasra on the bāʾ and sukūn on the rāʾ. He was born in the year 761 AH in Abiward, a town in Khurasan, to which his grandfather had moved, and he grew up there. He and his father were each known there as al-Khatib, hence he was called al-Khatibi. He studied sciences with a group of prominent scholars, and his father initially prevented him from occupying himself with rational sciences, then later permitted him, which delighted him. He closely associated with Sa‘d al-Taftazani in an excellent companionship. Then he traveled to Baghdad in the year 783 AH and studied there with Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Kurdi, author of al-Hawi fi al-Fiqh and al-Ghaya al-Quswa, and he closely associated with Shams al-Din al-Kirmani. Then he entered Yemen and met al-Nasir, who entrusted him with teaching at some schools in Ta‘izz, but death overtook him there in the year 816 AH. His works: 1 - A gloss on Sharh Matali‘ al-Anwar of al-Urmawi on logic and philosophy. 2 - Rabi‘ al-Jinan on al-Ma‘ani and al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for the first student of al-Taftazani, Husam al-Din al-Abiwardi. It begins by explaining the correct pronunciation of his name and then gives his birth year (761 AH) and birthplace (Abiward in Khurasan). It notes that both he and his father were known as 'al-Khatib', so he was called al-Khatibi. The passage then describes his educational journey: he initially studied various sciences under several great scholars, but his father forbade him from studying the rational sciences. Later his father allowed it, which greatly pleased him. He then became a close disciple of al-Taftazani. After that, he traveled to Baghdad in 783 AH, where he studied under Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Kurdi and closely associated with Shams al-Din al-Kirmani. Next, he went to Yemen and met al-Nasir, who appointed him as a teacher in some schools in Ta‘izz. He died there in 816 AH. Finally, the passage lists two of his works: a gloss on Sharh Matali‘ al-Anwar by al-Urmawi on logic and philosophy, and Rabi‘ al-Jinan on al-Ma‘ani and al-Bayan (rhetoric).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Today, identify one obstacle (internal or external) in your pursuit of knowledge and write down a concrete step you will take to overcome it.
?
Al-Abiwardi traveled from Khurasan to Baghdad to Yemen to study and teach. For the sake of gaining true understanding of your faith, what distance have you traveled—physically, mentally, or spiritually? If your answer is 'almost none,' ask yourself: what is holding you back? Is it comfort, fear, or lack of intention? Commit to one action this week that moves you out of your comfort zone for knowledge.
?
The passage says al-Abiwardi was 'delighted' when his father allowed him to study rational sciences. When was the last time you felt such pure joy at being permitted or able to learn something about Allah’s creation or His religion? Pray that Allah reinstills in you that delight, and then go seek it.

Biography of Ala al-Din al-Rumi: A Prodigious Hanafi Scholar
Introduces the third student of al-Taftazani, a Hanafi jurist and polymath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of Ala al-Din al-Rumi, including his lineage, scholarly achievements, and his study under the two giants al-Sharif and al-Taftazani.

Core Idea
Ala al-Din al-Rumi mastered debate by memorizing the sharp questions of his famous teachers.

This lesson introduces the third student of al-Taftazani, a Hanafi jurist and polymath. The passage from al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya provides a concise yet rich portrait of his scholarly lineage, birth date, and unique ability to absorb and reproduce the incisive debates of his teachers. Let's explore his biography.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the classical biographical style. Notice the structure: full name, birth year, scholarly attributes, teachers, and a quote.
The passage ends abruptly; the quote is incomplete.
2
Identify key biographical elements
Find the full name, birth year (756 AH), Hanafi affiliation, and his description as an outstanding jurist and polymath.
3
Understand his teachers and setting
He studied under al-Sharif (al-Jurjani) and Sa'd al-Taftazani. Their discussions took place in the presence of Timur (Tamerlane), indicating a high-profile academic environment.
This shows his access to the highest scholarly circles of his time.
4
Reflect on his special talent
He memorized and mastered the 'piercing questions and answers' from the debates. This highlights his sharp intellect and dedication.
The Arabic word 'مفحمة' implies questions that silence opponents.
5
Examine the concluding quote
The author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya describes him as 'knowledgeable, virtuous, and sharp'. The sentence is cut off, but it reinforces his intellectual caliber.

He was an outstanding jurist and versatile scholar. He studied under both al-Sharif (likely al-Sharif al-Jurjani) and Sa‘d al-Taftazani, and he attended their academic discussions in the presence of Timur and others. He was known for memorizing the incisive questions and answers from those sessions and mastering them. The passage ends with a quotation from the author of al-Shaqa’iq al-Nu‘maniyya, saying he was knowledgeable, virtuous, and ‘sharp’ (حديد), suggesting a sharp intellect, though the sentence is incomplete.

Ala' al-Din al-Rumi: A Scholar's Rise and Fall
Biographical entry covering origins, education, and court career.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life, education, and controversial career of 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi, including his relationship with Sultan al-Ashraf Barsbay.

Core Idea
A brilliant scholar with a sharp tongue and a chequered past.

The biography of 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi is a fascinating mix of scholarly excellence and personal scandal. This first part traces his origins, his training under great masters, and his rise and fall at the court of Sultan Barsbay. You will see how his sharp mind and even sharper temperament shaped his destiny.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice how the biography combines factual details with anecdotal accounts.
Pay attention to the names and dates mentioned.
2
Identify the key figures
Note the teachers (al-Taftazani, al-Jurjani) and patron (Sultan Barsbay). Understand the significance of these connections.
Al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani were two of the most prominent scholars of the era.
3
Analyze the incident with Barsbay
The passage describes how al-Rumi fell from favor. Identify the reasons given: financial misconduct and shameful acts. Then note his poetic plea for forgiveness.
The poem quotes a hadith to strengthen his apology.
4
Reflect on the poem's purpose
Consider why the biographer included the poem. It reveals al-Rumi's character and his relationship with the sultan.
The poem is not a theological argument but a biographical detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - علاء الدين الرومي : هو علاء الدين أبو الحسن علي بن مصلح الدين، موسى بن ابراهيم الرومي الحنفي الشيخ العلامة ولد سنة ست وخمسين وسبعمائة، وكان فقيهاً بارعاً مفنناً في علوم شتى، تخرج على الشريف والسعد التفتازاني وحضر أبحاثهما بحضرة تيمور وغيره فكان يحفظ تلك الأسئلة والأجوبة المفحمة ويتقنها (٤) . يقول عنه صاحب الشقائق النعمانية : كان رحمه الله عالماً فاضلا حديد الطبع قوي الذكاء والبحث حضر دروس العلامة التفتازاني والسيد الشريف الجرجاني ، له رسالة رحمه الله (۱) فيها الأسئلة من فنون شتى، وهي عندي بخط جدي جمع فيها الملك وقدم إلى مصر مرات كثيرة، ونال الحظوة والتكريم من الأشرف ،برسباى وولاه مشيخة الصوفية بمدرسته التي أنشأها فباشرها مدة ثم تركها . مات مصر وقيل أبعده عنها الملك الأشرف لكونه وضع يده على مال جزيل لبعض من من صوفيتها ولأمور فاحشة نقلت عنه (۲) فخرج من عمر متوجهاً إلى الحج ، وسافر من هناك إلى الروم، ثم عاد إلى الآخر سنة تسع وعشرين، وأنشد أمام الملك الأشرف : في ربيع إذا اعتذر الفقير إليـك يـومـاً تجاوز عن معاصيه الكثيرة فإن الشافعي روى حديثاً بإسناد صحيح عن مغيرة عن المختار: أن الله يمحو بعذر واحد ألفي كبيرة يقول عنه صاحب الضوء اللامع : وكان متضلعاً من العلوم ممن حضر في الابتداء مناظرات التفتازاني والسيد بحضرة الوالي وغيره فحفظ تلك الأسئلة والأجوبة الفخمة ،وأتقنها، غير أنه كان مبغضاً للناس لطيشه وحدة مزاجة وجرأته واستخفافه بمن يبحث معه . = قال العيني : كان عالماً محققاً بحاثاً ديناً. وقال المقريزي في عقوده وغيرها : كان فاضلا في عدة علوم مع طيش وخفة وجرأة بلسانه على مالا يليق . مات سنة إحدى وأربعين وثمانمائة ودفن بمقبرة باب النصر بالقاهرة (۳)
3 - 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi: He is 'Ala' al-Din Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muslih al-Din, Musa ibn Ibrahim al-Rumi al-Hanafi, the shaykh, the scholar, born in the year 756 AH. He was an outstanding jurist, versatile in various sciences, studied under al-Sharif and Sa'd al-Taftazani, and attended their debates in the presence of Timur and others, and he would memorize those decisive questions and answers and master them (4). The author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya says about him: 'He was, may God have mercy on him, a virtuous scholar, sharp-natured, strong in intelligence and research, attended the lessons of the scholar al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani. He had a treatise, may God have mercy on him (1), containing questions from various disciplines, and it is with me in the handwriting of my grandfather, in which he collected [material] about the king. He went to Egypt many times, and obtained favor and honor from al-Ashraf Barsbay, who appointed him head of the Sufis at his school which he had founded, and he managed it for a while then left it. He died in Egypt, and it is said that al-Ashraf expelled him because he had laid his hand on a large amount of money belonging to some of its Sufis and for shameful matters reported about him (2). So he left 'Umar heading for Hajj, traveled from there to Rum, then returned to the other in the year 29 [i.e. 829?], and recited before al-Ashraf: 'In spring, if the poor one apologizes to you one day, you overlook his many sins, for indeed al-Shafi'i narrated a hadith with a sound chain from Mughira from al-Mukhtar: That God erases two thousand major sins with a single excuse.' The author of al-Daw' al-Lami' says about him: 'He was deeply learned in the sciences, having attended in the beginning the debates of al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid in the presence of the governor and others, and he memorized those magnificent questions and answers and mastered them, but he was hateful to people due to his rashness, sharp temper, audacity, and his belittling of those who debated with him.' = Al-'Ayni said: 'He was a profound scholar, a researcher, religious.' Al-Maqrizi said in his 'Uqud and elsewhere: 'He was virtuous in several sciences, with rashness, lightness, and audacity of tongue regarding what is improper.' He died in the year 841 AH and was buried in the cemetery of Bab al-Nasr in Cairo (3).
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biographical entry for 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi (full name: 'Ala' al-Din Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muslih al-Din, Musa ibn Ibrahim al-Rumi al-Hanafi). It begins with his birth year (756 AH) and describes him as an outstanding jurist and versatile scholar. He studied under al-Sharif and Sa'd al-Taftazani and attended their debates before Timur. The passage then quotes from various historians: first, the author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya praises his intelligence but notes his sharp nature, and mentions that he had a treatise containing questions from various disciplines, which the author possesses in his grandfather's handwriting. It relates his travels to Egypt, his favor with Sultan al-Ashraf Barsbay, who appointed him head of Sufis, but later expelled him due to financial misconduct and other shameful acts. The passage includes a poem he recited before the sultan seeking forgiveness, citing a hadith from al-Shafi'i. Next, al-Daw' al-Lami' describes him as deeply learned but hateful to people due to his rashness and audacity. Al-'Ayni testifies to his profound scholarship and religiosity. Al-Maqrizi confirms his virtues but notes his rashness and impropriety. Finally, his death in 841 AH and burial in Cairo are recorded.

Key Terms
علاء الدين الرومي
التفتازاني
السيد الشريف الجرجاني
الأشرف برسباى
الشقائق النعمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The poem and hadith quoted in this passage are often taken as theological proof or a valid argument in kalam.
Correction: The poem and hadith are quoted as part of the biography to illustrate al-Rumi's character and his attempt to gain forgiveness from the sultan, not as a doctrinal proof. Do not extract a kalam argument from this passage.

Checkpoint
Under which sultan did 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi obtain a position as head of Sufis?
A) Timur
B) al-Ashraf Barsbay
C) al-Maqrizi
D) al-Sayyid al-Sharif

Key Takeaway
'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi was a brilliant scholar who rose to a high position under Sultan Barsbay but fell due to misconduct, as recounted in a detailed biographical entry with a poetic plea for forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi, a brilliant scholar, was expelled for taking money and for 'shameful matters', do you see any of his arrogance or entitlement in your own heart? What makes you think you are above such falls?
?
He recited a poem before the sultan citing a hadith that God erases two thousand major sins with a single excuse. Are you using God's mercy as a license to sin, hoping that a quick apology will erase everything while you continue in wrongdoing?
?
Consider the tale of his life: he rose high, fell low, then sought forgiveness with poetry. If you were in his place, would you truly repent or would you too try to charm your way back into favor? What does your answer reveal about your relationship with Allah?

Scholarly Assessments of Ala' al-Din al-Rumi
Quotations from three historians assessing al-Rumi's character and scholarship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three different historians assessed the character and scholarship of 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi.

Core Idea
Historians agree on his brilliance but differ on his character.

The second part of the biography presents the evaluations of three historians: al-Daw' al-Lami', al-'Ayni, and al-Maqrizi. Each offers a slightly different perspective on al-Rumi's scholarship and temperament. Read how they balance praise with criticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three distinct voices: al-Daw' al-Lami', al-'Ayni, and al-Maqrizi.
Each quote is attributed to a specific author.
2
Compare the assessments
Al-Daw' al-Lami' emphasizes his deep learning but harsh temperament. Al-'Ayni focuses on his religiosity. Al-Maqrizi mentions his virtues but also his rashness. Note how they agree and differ.
Look for the common theme of sharpness and audacity.
3
Understand the overall portrait
The combined testimonies paint a complex picture: a highly learned man with a difficult personality. Consider why the biographer included all three.
This reflects the scholarly tradition of providing multiple witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - علاء الدين الرومي : هو علاء الدين أبو الحسن علي بن مصلح الدين، موسى بن ابراهيم الرومي الحنفي الشيخ العلامة ولد سنة ست وخمسين وسبعمائة، وكان فقيهاً بارعاً مفنناً في علوم شتى، تخرج على الشريف والسعد التفتازاني وحضر أبحاثهما بحضرة تيمور وغيره فكان يحفظ تلك الأسئلة والأجوبة المفحمة ويتقنها (٤) . يقول عنه صاحب الشقائق النعمانية : كان رحمه الله عالماً فاضلا حديد الطبع قوي الذكاء والبحث حضر دروس العلامة التفتازاني والسيد الشريف الجرجاني ، له رسالة رحمه الله (۱) فيها الأسئلة من فنون شتى، وهي عندي بخط جدي جمع فيها الملك وقدم إلى مصر مرات كثيرة، ونال الحظوة والتكريم من الأشرف ،برسباى وولاه مشيخة الصوفية بمدرسته التي أنشأها فباشرها مدة ثم تركها . مات مصر وقيل أبعده عنها الملك الأشرف لكونه وضع يده على مال جزيل لبعض من من صوفيتها ولأمور فاحشة نقلت عنه (۲) فخرج من عمر متوجهاً إلى الحج ، وسافر من هناك إلى الروم، ثم عاد إلى الآخر سنة تسع وعشرين، وأنشد أمام الملك الأشرف : في ربيع إذا اعتذر الفقير إليـك يـومـاً تجاوز عن معاصيه الكثيرة فإن الشافعي روى حديثاً بإسناد صحيح عن مغيرة عن المختار: أن الله يمحو بعذر واحد ألفي كبيرة يقول عنه صاحب الضوء اللامع : وكان متضلعاً من العلوم ممن حضر في الابتداء مناظرات التفتازاني والسيد بحضرة الوالي وغيره فحفظ تلك الأسئلة والأجوبة الفخمة ،وأتقنها، غير أنه كان مبغضاً للناس لطيشه وحدة مزاجة وجرأته واستخفافه بمن يبحث معه . = قال العيني : كان عالماً محققاً بحاثاً ديناً. وقال المقريزي في عقوده وغيرها : كان فاضلا في عدة علوم مع طيش وخفة وجرأة بلسانه على مالا يليق . مات سنة إحدى وأربعين وثمانمائة ودفن بمقبرة باب النصر بالقاهرة (۳)
3 - 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi: He is 'Ala' al-Din Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muslih al-Din, Musa ibn Ibrahim al-Rumi al-Hanafi, the shaykh, the scholar, born in the year 756 AH. He was an outstanding jurist, versatile in various sciences, studied under al-Sharif and Sa'd al-Taftazani, and attended their debates in the presence of Timur and others, and he would memorize those decisive questions and answers and master them (4). The author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya says about him: 'He was, may God have mercy on him, a virtuous scholar, sharp-natured, strong in intelligence and research, attended the lessons of the scholar al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani. He had a treatise, may God have mercy on him (1), containing questions from various disciplines, and it is with me in the handwriting of my grandfather, in which he collected [material] about the king. He went to Egypt many times, and obtained favor and honor from al-Ashraf Barsbay, who appointed him head of the Sufis at his school which he had founded, and he managed it for a while then left it. He died in Egypt, and it is said that al-Ashraf expelled him because he had laid his hand on a large amount of money belonging to some of its Sufis and for shameful matters reported about him (2). So he left 'Umar heading for Hajj, traveled from there to Rum, then returned to the other in the year 29 [i.e. 829?], and recited before al-Ashraf: 'In spring, if the poor one apologizes to you one day, you overlook his many sins, for indeed al-Shafi'i narrated a hadith with a sound chain from Mughira from al-Mukhtar: That God erases two thousand major sins with a single excuse.' The author of al-Daw' al-Lami' says about him: 'He was deeply learned in the sciences, having attended in the beginning the debates of al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid in the presence of the governor and others, and he memorized those magnificent questions and answers and mastered them, but he was hateful to people due to his rashness, sharp temper, audacity, and his belittling of those who debated with him.' = Al-'Ayni said: 'He was a profound scholar, a researcher, religious.' Al-Maqrizi said in his 'Uqud and elsewhere: 'He was virtuous in several sciences, with rashness, lightness, and audacity of tongue regarding what is improper.' He died in the year 841 AH and was buried in the cemetery of Bab al-Nasr in Cairo (3).
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biographical entry for 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi (full name: 'Ala' al-Din Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muslih al-Din, Musa ibn Ibrahim al-Rumi al-Hanafi). It begins with his birth year (756 AH) and describes him as an outstanding jurist and versatile scholar. He studied under al-Sharif and Sa'd al-Taftazani and attended their debates before Timur. The passage then quotes from various historians: first, the author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya praises his intelligence but notes his sharp nature, and mentions that he had a treatise containing questions from various disciplines, which the author possesses in his grandfather's handwriting. It relates his travels to Egypt, his favor with Sultan al-Ashraf Barsbay, who appointed him head of Sufis, but later expelled him due to financial misconduct and other shameful acts. The passage includes a poem he recited before the sultan seeking forgiveness, citing a hadith from al-Shafi'i. Next, al-Daw' al-Lami' describes him as deeply learned but hateful to people due to his rashness and audacity. Al-'Ayni testifies to his profound scholarship and religiosity. Al-Maqrizi confirms his virtues but notes his rashness and impropriety. Finally, his death in 841 AH and burial in Cairo are recorded.

Key Terms

العيني
المقريزي

Key Takeaway
Historians of the time offered contrasting assessments of 'Ala' al-Din al-Rumi, praising his scholarship but differing on his character, with some focusing on his religiosity and others on his sharp temper.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If historians were to record your conduct in debates or disagreements, what would they write about your temper and treatment of others? How does al-Rumi's example challenge you to pursue knowledge with humility?
?
Al-Rumi was deeply learned but his sharp temper is still remembered centuries later. What do you want to be remembered for: your knowledge alone, or how you treated people? Which historian's assessment would you want written about you?
?
Think of a recent situation where you felt the urge to belittle someone in an argument. How can you apply the lesson of al-Rumi's mixed legacy to choose respect over rashness, even when you are certain you are right?

A Scholar of the Taftazani-Jurjani Circle: Biography and Contradictory Assessments
Biography of a scholar from the Taftazani-Jurjani circle with multiple evaluations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and character of a scholar from the circle of al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani, as seen through multiple contemporary sources.

Core Idea
Even great scholars can be both deeply learned and deeply flawed.

This lesson presents the biography of a scholar who studied under two of the most famous theologians of the late Timurid period, al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani. Through the eyes of his biographers, we see a man of sharp intellect but troubling character, whose life reflects the complexities of scholarly achievement and human weakness.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full story of this scholar's life.
Pay attention to the sequence of events and the different voices quoted.
2
Identify the different perspectives
Notice how the author, al-'Ayni, and al-Maqrizi each evaluate the scholar. What are the key points of agreement and disagreement?
3
Analyze the contradictions
Why do these accounts differ? Consider the possible biases or contexts of each biographer.
4
Reflect on the lesson
What does this biography teach us about the relationship between knowledge and character?
Think about the ideal of 'ilm versus personal conduct.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطبع قوي الذكاء والبحث حضر دروس العلامة التفتازاني والسيد الشريف الجرجاني ، له رسالة رحمه الله (١) فيها الأسئلة من فنون شتى، وهي عندي بخط جدي جمع فيها الملك وقدم إلى مصر مرات كثيرة، ونال الحظوة والتكريم من الأشرف برسباى وولاه مشيخة الصوفية بمدرسته التي أنشأها فباشرها مدة ثم تركها . مات مصر وقيل أبعده عنها الملك الأشرف لكونه وضع يده على مال جزيل لبعض من صوفيتها ولأمور فاحشة نقلت عنه (٢) فخرج من عمر متوجهاً إلى الحج ، وسافر من هناك إلى الروم، ثم عاد إلى الآخر سنة تسع وعشرين، وأنشد أمام الملك الأشرف : في ربيع إذا اعتذر الفقير إليـك يـومـاً تجاوز عن معاصيه الكثيرة فإن الشافعي روى حديثاً بإسناد صحيح عن مغيرة عن المختار: أن الله يمحو بعذر واحد ألفي كبيرة يقول عنه صاحب الضوء اللامع : وكان متضلعاً من العلوم ممن حضر في الابتداء مناظرات التفتازاني والسيد بحضرة الوالي وغيره فحفظ تلك الأسئلة والأجوبة الفخمة ،وأتقنها، غير أنه كان مبغضاً للناس لطيشه وحدة مزاجة وجرأته واستخفافه بمن يبحث معه . = قال العيني : كان عالماً محققاً بحاثاً ديناً. وقال المقريزي في عقوده وغيرها : كان فاضلا في عدة علوم مع طيش وخفة وجرأة بلسانه على مالا يليق . مات سنة إحدى وأربعين وثمانمائة ودفن بمقبرة باب النصر بالقاهرة (٣)
By nature strong in intelligence and research, he attended the lessons of the eminent scholar al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani. He had a treatise, may God have mercy on him (1), containing questions from various arts, and it is with me in the handwriting of my grandfather. In it he collected the king and came to Egypt many times, and obtained favor and honor from al-Ashraf Barsbay, who appointed him as the shaykh of the Sufis at his school which he had established. He supervised it for a while then left it. He died in Egypt, and it was said that al-Ashraf expelled him from it because he had laid his hand on a large amount of money belonging to some of its Sufis and for obscene matters reported about him (2). So he left Egypt heading for the Hajj, and traveled from there to Anatolia, then returned to the other in the year twenty-nine, and recited before al-Ashraf: 'In spring, if the poor man apologizes to you one day, you overlook his many sins. For al-Shafi'i narrated a hadith with a sound chain from Mughira from al-Mukhtar that God erases two thousand major sins with a single excuse.' The author of al-Daw' al-Lami' says about him: He was deeply learned in the sciences, among those who initially attended the debates of al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid in the presence of the governor and others, so he memorized those magnificent questions and answers and mastered them. However, he was hateful to people due to his recklessness, sharpness of temperament, audacity, and his contempt for those who debated with him. = al-'Ayni said: He was a scholar, investigator, researcher, religious. And al-Maqrizi said in his 'Uqud and elsewhere: He was excellent in several sciences, with recklessness, lightness, and audacity of tongue for what is not proper. He died in the year 841 AH and was buried in the Bab al-Nasr cemetery in Cairo (3).
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a biography of an unnamed scholar from the circle of al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani. It begins by describing his natural intelligence and his attendance of the lessons of these two great scholars. He authored a treatise containing questions from various disciplines, which the author of this biographical entry possesses in his grandfather's handwriting. The scholar enjoyed the favor of the Mamluk sultan al-Ashraf Barsbay, who appointed him as the shaykh of the Sufis at a school the sultan had built. However, he was later expelled from Egypt, allegedly for misappropriating funds and for immoral acts. He then left for Hajj, traveled to Anatolia, and returned at a later date. While before the sultan, he recited a poem citing a hadith from al-Shafi'i about God's forgiveness. The author of al-Daw' al-Lami' praises his deep learning and his mastery of the debates he witnessed, but also criticizes his unpleasant character—being reckless, sharp-tongued, and contemptuous of others. The passage then quotes two other scholars: al-'Ayni gives a positive assessment ('a scholar, investigator, researcher, religious'), while al-Maqrizi acknowledges his learning but notes his recklessness and inappropriate speech. The biography concludes with his death date (841 AH) and burial place in Cairo.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge does not always come with good character; the scholars of the past were complex individuals whose lives must be understood in context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a religious scholar with a scandalous reputation, do you automatically reject their knowledge, or do you try to separate the message from the messenger? This lesson forces you to examine your own tendency to idolize or demonize learned people. How will you hold onto the benefit of their knowledge while acknowledging their humanity?
?
The scholar recited a poem before the sultan, citing a hadith that God erases two thousand major sins with a single excuse. Have you ever used the hope of divine forgiveness as a license to persist in sin, rather than as a motivation to repent? What would it look like for you to truly internalize both God's mercy and your personal responsibility?
?
The assessments of this scholar are deeply contradictory: one praises him as 'religious' (dīnan), another calls him reckless and audacious. Who are you when no one is watching? Whose evaluation would you fear most—and why? Are you willing to let the complexity of this scholar's life challenge your own self-deception?

Biography of 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Bukhārī
Biography of 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Bukhārī: education, travels, and character

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, education, travels, and character of the Hanafi scholar 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Bukhārī.

Core Idea
A life of learning, asceticism, and influence across the Islamic world.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid introduces a towering Hanafi scholar of the 8th/14th century. Al-Bukhārī's biography illustrates the ideal of a scholar who combined deep knowledge of both transmitted and rational sciences with unwavering piety. Understanding his life helps us appreciate the scholarly networks that shaped later Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overall sense of the biography. Notice the sequence of events and the qualities highlighted.
2
Identify key life stages
Go through the biography and note the major phases: birth, early education, study under al-Taftazani, travels to India, Mecca, Egypt, and Syria, and his death.
Pay attention to the places and their significance.
3
Reflect on his character and legacy
Consider the descriptions of his asceticism, piety, his relationship with rulers, and his dedication to enjoining good. How does this portrait fit the ideal scholar of his time?
The eulogy at the end summarizes his lasting impact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - علاء الدين البخاري: هو علاء الدين محمد بن محمد بن محمد محمد البخاري العجمي الحنفي العلامة، علامة الوقت. وقال ابن حجر ولد سنة تسع وسبعين وسبعمائة ببلاد العجم ونشأ ببخارى فنفقه بأبيه وعمه العلاء عبد الرحمن . وأخذ الأدبيات والعقليات عن السعد التفتازاني وغيره، ورحل إلى الأقطار واجتهد في الأخذ عن العلماء حتى برع في المعقول والمنقول والمفهوم والمنطوق واللغة العربية وصار إمام عصره، وتوجه إلى الهند فاستوطنه مدة، وعظم أمره عند ملوكه إلى الغاية، لما شاهدوه من غزير علمه وزهده وورعه . ثم قدم مكة فأقام بها، ودخل مصر فاستوطنها وتصدر للاقرار بها فأخذ عنه غالب من أدركناه من كل مذهب، وانتفعوا به علماً وجاهاً ومالاً . ونال عظمة بالقاهرة مع عدم تردد إلى أحد من أعيانها، حتى ولا السلطان، والكل يحضر إليه، وكان ملازماً للاشتغال والأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. والقيام بذات الله تعالى ضعف كان يعتريه وآل أمره إلى أن توجه إلى الشام مع فسار إليها بعد أن سأله السلطان الإقامة بمصر مراراً فلم يقبل، وفي الشام أقام مات رحمه الله في خامس شهر رمضان ولم يخلف بعده مثله في العلم والزهد والورع ، وإقماع أهل الظلم والجور (١)
4 - 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Bukhārī: He is 'Alā' al-Dīn Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad Muḥammad al-Bukhārī al-'Ajamī al-Ḥanafī, the scholar, the scholar of the time. Ibn Ḥajar said: He was born in the year 779 AH in the lands of the non-Arabs and grew up in Bukhara, and he gained understanding of jurisprudence from his father and his uncle al-'Alā' 'Abd al-Raḥmān. He studied literary and rational sciences under al-Sa'd al-Taftazānī and others, and traveled to various regions and strove in taking from scholars until he excelled in rational and transmitted knowledge, understood and spoken, and the Arabic language, and became the imam of his age. He headed to India and settled there for a while, and his status became extremely great with its kings, due to what they witnessed of his abundant knowledge, asceticism, and piety. Then he came to Mecca and stayed there, and entered Egypt and settled there and took the lead in teaching, so that most of those we met from every madhhab took from him and benefited from him in knowledge, status, and wealth. He attained grandeur in Cairo without frequenting any of its notables, not even the sultan, and everyone came to him. He was constantly engaged in study and enjoining good and forbidding evil. He had a weakness in his body, and his affair ended with him heading to Syria, where he went after the sultan repeatedly asked him to stay in Egypt but he refused. He settled in Syria and died, may God have mercy on him, on the fifth of Ramadan, and he left none after him like him in knowledge, asceticism, piety, and silencing the people of oppression and injustice (1).
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the Hanafi scholar 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Bukhārī. It begins by giving his full name and lineage, noting his origin from Bukhara and his Hanafi affiliation. His birth year (779 AH) is cited from Ibn Hajar. He grew up in Bukhara and studied fiqh under his father and uncle, then took literary and rational sciences from al-Taftazani and others. He traveled widely, excelling in both transmitted and rational sciences as well as Arabic, becoming a leading scholar of his time. He sojourned in India, where kings honored him for his knowledge and piety. He then moved to Mecca and eventually settled in Cairo, where he taught and attracted students from all madhhabs, benefiting them in knowledge, status, and wealth. Despite not visiting any notables (even the sultan), people flocked to him. He was diligent in study and moral command. He suffered from a physical weakness. After the sultan repeatedly asked him to stay in Egypt, he refused and moved to Syria, where he died on the fifth of Ramadan. The biography ends with praise: he left no one like him in knowledge, asceticism, piety, and in silencing wrongdoers.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about a scholar who refused the sultan's request to stay in Egypt and instead went to Syria, despite his weakness. What attachments in your own life would you be unwilling to give up for the sake of your faith? Will you examine your heart today to see if any of these attachments have become idols?
?
This scholar was known for not frequenting the powerful; rather, they came to him. How often do you seek the approval of those in authority or status, hoping to gain something from them? What would it take for you to live with such independence for the sake of Allah?
?
He was constant in enjoining good and forbidding evil, even as his body weakened. When was the last time you spoke out against an injustice or sin you witnessed, even when it was uncomfortable? Are you willing to commit to speaking truth to power, starting with one small act this week?

Biography of Ḥaydar al-Rūmī: Origins, Teachers, and Travels
Biography of the Hanafi-Rifa'i scholar Ḥaydar al-Rūmī: origins, teachers, and travels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the background and significance of the Hanafi-Rifa'i scholar Ḥaydar al-Rūmī, including his origins, teachers, travels, and connections to major scholars of his time.

Core Idea
Ḥaydar al-Rūmī was a well-traveled Hanafi-Rifa'i scholar who met al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani.

This lesson introduces you to a lesser-known yet fascinating figure from the 8th/14th century: Ḥaydar al-Rūmī. Though his name may not be as famous as his contemporaries, his biography reveals a scholar deeply connected to the intellectual networks of his time. The passage gives us a glimpse into his origins, his travels, and his encounters with two giants of Islamic scholarship: al-Taftazānī and al-Sayyid al-Jurjānī.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the dense packaging of information in a few lines.
2
Identify the key elements
List the following: his full name, his titles, his origin, place of birth, teachers, travels, the scholars he met, and his arrival in Cairo.
This will help you structure the information.
3
Consider the significance of his meetings
Reflect on what it means that al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani met him. These are two of the most influential scholars in the later Islamic intellectual tradition. What does this say about Ḥaydar's own standing?
Think about scholarly networks in the 8th/14th century.
4
Reflect on the incomplete date
The passage ends with 'he came to Cairo in the year four (1).' This is a common feature in biographical literature where the exact year is abbreviated or left incomplete. Consider how scholars later filled in such gaps.
This illustrates the transmission of biographical data.

ه - حيدر الرومي : هو حيدر بن أحمد بن ابراهيم أبو الحسن الرومي الأصل العجمي الحنفي الرفاعي نزيل القاهرة، ويعرف بشيخ التاج والسبع وجوه . ولد بشيراز في حدود الثمانين وسبعمائة وقرأ على أبيه وغيره، ورحل إلى البلاد، ووفد على ملوك الشمس وعلمائه . وكان ممن اجتمع به التفتازاني والسيد الجرجاني. وقدم القاهرة سنة أربع (١)
H - Ḥaydar al-Rūmī: He is Ḥaydar ibn Aḥmad ibn Ibrāhīm Abū al-Ḥasan, of Rūmī origin, non-Arab, Ḥanafī, al-Rifā'ī, resident of Cairo, and known as Shaykh al-Tāj and al-Sab' Wujūh. He was born in Shiraz around the year 780 AH and studied under his father and others, traveled to various lands, and visited the kings of the sun [meaning: sultans?] and their scholars. He was among those with whom al-Taftazānī and al-Sayyid al-Jurjānī met. He came to Cairo in the year four (1).
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a short biography of Ḥaydar al-Rūmī, a Hanafi-Rifa'i scholar. It provides his full name, lineage, and titles: he is known as Shaykh al-Tāj and al-Sab' Wujūh (meaning 'the seven faces'? possibly a nickname). He was originally from Anatolia (Rūm) but born in Shiraz around 780 AH. He studied under his father and others, traveled widely, and visited sultans and scholars. Notably, he was a contemporary of al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani, as he met them. The biography ends with his arrival in Cairo in the year four, likely meaning 804 AH or another year, but the exact year is not fully given here (the footnote provides his death year).

Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari: A Model of Knowledge and Piety
Biographical account of Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari's life and virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly journey, and key virtues of Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari as recorded in the biographical tradition.

Core Idea
Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari combined deep learning, asceticism, and fearless moral leadership.

This passage introduces one of the towering Hanafi scholars of the 9th century, Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari. The biography traces his intellectual formation under his father and uncle, his studies with the famous Saad al-Din al-Taftazani, his travels across the Islamic world, and his eventual settlement in Syria. The text emphasizes his mastery of both transmitted and rational sciences, his independence from rulers, and his relentless commitment to commanding good and forbidding evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the chain of teachers, travels, and the author's praise.
The passage uses Ibn Hajar as an authority for the early details.
2
Identify the key phases of his life
List the major stages: birth, education, travels to India, Mecca, Egypt, and Syria. See how each location contributed to his scholarly growth.
3
Note his distinguishing qualities
The text highlights his knowledge, asceticism (zuhd), piety (wara'), and courage in commanding good and forbidding evil. Reflect on how these qualities earned him respect from kings and commoners alike.
4
Examine his relationship with political power
Al-Bukhari did not visit the sultan or nobles; they came to him. Consider the significance of this independence for a scholar of his stature.
This contrasts with some scholars who sought royal patronage.
5
Summarise his legacy
The passage ends by stating no one like him remained after his death. Summarise why he was unique in knowledge, zuhd, and opposition to injustice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - علاء الدين البخاري: هو علاء الدين محمد بن محمد بن محمد البخاري العجمي الحنفي العلامة، علامة الوقت. قال ابن حجر: ولد سنة تسع وسبعين وسبعمائة ببلاد العجم ونشأ ببخارى فتفقه بأبيه وعمه العلاء عبد الرحمن. وأخذ الأدبيات والعقليات عن السعد التفتازاني وغيره، ورحل إلى الأقطار واجتهد في الأخذ عن العلماء حتى برع في المعقول والمنقول والمفهوم والمنطوق واللغة العربية وصار إمام عصره، وتوجه إلى الهند فاستوطنه مدة، وعظم أمره عند ملوكه إلى الغاية، لما شاهدوه من غزير علمه وزهده وورعه. ثم قدم مكة فأقام بها، ودخل مصر فاستوطنها وتصدر للإقراء بها فأخذ عنه غالب من أدركناه من كل مذهب، وانتفعوا به علماً وجاهاً ومالاً. ونال عظمة بالقاهرة مع عدم تردده إلى أحد من أعيانها، حتى ولا السلطان، والكل يحضر إليه، وكان ملازماً للاشتغال والأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، والقيام بذات الله تعالى. ضعف كان يعتريه وآل أمره إلى أن توجه إلى الشام وسار إليها بعد أن سأله السلطان الإقامة بمصر مراراً فلم يقبل، وفي الشام أقام ومات رحمه الله في خامس شهر رمضان، ولم يخلف بعده مثله في العلم والزهد والورع، وإقماع أهل الظلم والجور (١).
4 - Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari: He is Alaa al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bukhari al-Ajami al-Hanafi, the eminent scholar, the marvel of his time. Ibn Hajar said: He was born in the year 779 AH in the lands of the non-Arabs and grew up in Bukhara, and he studied jurisprudence with his father and his uncle Alaa Abd al-Rahman. He studied the literary and rational sciences with Saad al-Din al-Taftazani and others, and he journeyed to the regions and strove in learning from scholars until he excelled in the rational and transmitted sciences, the abstract and the articulated, and the Arabic language, and he became the imam of his time. He then went to India and settled there for a time, and his status became extremely great with its kings, due to what they witnessed of his abundant knowledge, asceticism, and piety. Then he came to Mecca and resided there, and he entered Egypt and settled there, and he took charge of teaching there, and most of those we encountered from every school of law studied under him and benefited from him in knowledge, social standing, and wealth. He attained grandeur in Cairo without visiting any of its notables, not even the sultan, and everyone would come to him. He was constant in his scholarly pursuits, commanding good and forbidding evil, and standing up for the sake of Allah Almighty. He suffered from a weakness, and his situation ended with him heading to Syria, and he traveled there after the sultan asked him repeatedly to stay in Egypt but he did not accept. And in Syria he settled and died, may Allah have mercy on him, on the fifth of Ramadan, and there remained no one after him like him in knowledge, asceticism, piety, and subduing the people of injustice and tyranny.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for the Hanafi scholar Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari. It begins by naming him and praising him as an eminent scholar and marvel of his time. It then cites Ibn Hajar for his birth date (779 AH) and upbringing in Bukhara, where he studied jurisprudence under his father and uncle. He studied the literary and rational sciences under al-Taftazani, travelled widely to learn from scholars, and mastered both the rational and transmitted sciences as well as Arabic. He became the leading imam of his time. He then moved to India, where he was highly esteemed by the rulers for his knowledge, asceticism, and piety. After that he went to Mecca, then to Egypt, where he taught; many students from all schools studied with him and benefited. Despite his high position in Cairo, he did not visit any of the elite, not even the sultan; rather, they came to him. He was devoted to scholarship and enjoining good and forbidding evil, standing up for God. Due to a physical weakness, he eventually moved to Syria after repeatedly refusing the sultan's request to stay in Egypt. He died in Syria on the fifth of Ramadan, and the passage concludes that no one equal to him in knowledge, asceticism, piety, and opposition to injustice remained.

علامة الوقت
التفتازاني
الإقراء
الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ibn Hajar
B) Saad al-Din al-Taftazani
C) His father

Key Takeaway
Alaa al-Din al-Bukhari exemplified the ideal scholar: deeply learned, ascetic, independent of worldly power, and courageous in commanding good and forbidding evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to seek knowledge, but are you willing to stand up for the truth even if it means displeasing those in authority? How does al-Bukhari's example challenge your comfort zone?
?
Al-Bukhari did not visit the sultan; the sultan came to him. Are you more concerned with being seen by people of influence than with earning Allah's pleasure? What would it take for you to prioritize Allah's pleasure over human recognition?
?
He combined asceticism with active engagement in society. Are you using your knowledge to serve others, or do you hide behind your studies to avoid responsibility? What one concrete step can you take this week to enjoin good or forbid evil in your environment?

Biography of Haydar al-Rumi
Biographical entry for Haydar al-Rumi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life of the Hanafi scholar Haydar al-Rumi, his travels, and his role as a shaykh in Mamluk Cairo.

Core Idea
Haydar al-Rumi's life shows the movement of scholars and their ties to rulers in the 15th-century Islamic world.

In this biographical passage, Sanusi introduces us to a contemporary scholar of the 9th/15th century, Haydar al-Rumi. The text not only gives his lineage and places of travel but also highlights his connections with major scholars like al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Jurjani. This brief life story illustrates the scholarly networks that linked Anatolia, Iran, Syria, and Egypt, as well as the patronage of Mamluk rulers.

Guided Path
1
Read the full biography
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the sequence of events: his birth, studies, travel, meeting scholars, arrival in Cairo, and later career.
2
Identify the key figures he met
The passage mentions he met al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Jurjani. These are two prominent scholars of the time, known for their works on theology and logic. Consider why this is noteworthy.
Al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani were major authorities in the rational sciences.
3
Examine his relations with Mamluk rulers
He was hosted by al-Ashraf and later had a dispute with al-Zahir Jaqmaq. This shows the importance of political support and the precarious position of scholars.
4
Note his appointment at Qubbat al-Nasr
He succeeded Mahmud al-Isbahani as shaykh of a famous Sufi lodge. This role combined teaching and spiritual guidance.
Qubbat al-Nasr was a prominent center in Cairo.
5
Reflect on the significance of his death and burial
He died at about seventy and was buried at Bab al-Wazir. Think about what this tells us about the scholarly community in Cairo.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥ - حيدر الرومي: هو حيدر بن أحمد بن إبراهيم أبو الحسن الرومي الأصل العجمي الحنفي الرفاعي نزيل القاهرة، ويعرف بشيخ التاج والسبع وجوه. ولد بشيراز في حدود الثمانين وسبعمائة وقرأ على أبيه وغيره، ورحل إلى البلاد، ووفد على ملوك الشام وعلمائه. وكان ممن اجتمع به التفتازاني والسيد الجرجاني. وقدم القاهرة سنة أربع وعشرين بأخويه إبراهيم الشاب الظريف والموله حيران وأمهم، فأكرم الأشرف وفادتهم وأنزله المنظرة المشار إليها وأنعم عليه، واقتطعه الأراضي، حدثت له جفوة مع الظاهر جقمق ولكن ما لبث أن استرضاه. تولى مشيخة قبة النصر بعد صرف محمود الأصبهاني منها، وسكنها إلى أن مرض وطال مرضه ثم مات ليلة الاثنين حادي عشر ربيع الأول سنة أربع وخمسين وثمانمائة عن نحو السبعين ودفن بباب الوزير (١).
5 - Haydar al-Rumi: He is Haydar ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim Abu al-Hasan, of Rumi origin, of non-Arab origin, the Hanafi al-Rifai, resident of Cairo, and known as Shaykh al-Taj and the seven faces. He was born in Shiraz around the year 780 AH and studied under his father and others, and he traveled to the lands, and visited the kings of Syria and its scholars. Among those he met were al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Jurjani. He came to Cairo in the year 824 with his two brothers, Ibrahim the handsome youth and the bewildered Hayran, and their mother. Al-Ashraf honored their visit and housed them in the aforementioned lookout and bestowed favors upon him, and granted him lands. A coolness occurred between him and al-Zahir Jaqmaq, but he soon appeased him. He assumed the position of shaykh of Qubbat al-Nasr after the dismissal of Mahmud al-Isbahani, and lived there until he fell ill and his illness lasted long, then he died on the night of Monday, the 11th of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 854 AH, at about seventy years of age, and was buried at Bab al-Wazir.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Haydar al-Rumi, a Hanafi scholar of Rumi (Anatolian) origin, affiliated with the Rifai order. It gives his full name and epithet 'Shaykh al-Taj and the seven faces' (perhaps referring to multiple scholarly specialties). He was born in Shiraz around 780 AH, studied under his father, and travelled widely, meeting scholars including al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Jurjani. He arrived in Cairo in 824 AH with his two brothers and mother, and was well received by the ruler al-Ashraf, who granted him a residence and land. He later had a disagreement with another ruler, al-Zahir Jaqmaq, but reconciled. He became the head of the Qubbat al-Nasr (Dome of Victory), a Sufi lodge, after the previous shaykh was dismissed. He lived there until a prolonged illness, and died in 854 AH at about seventy. He was buried at Bab al-Wazir.

التفتازاني
السيد الجرجاني
قبة النصر
شيخ التاج

Key Takeaway

?
In his final years, Haydar lived in a Sufi lodge, ill and waiting for death. If you knew that you would soon die, would you be satisfied with how you spent your life? What changes must you make so that your last days are filled with devotion rather than regret?

Biography of Alaa al-Din Ali al-Qawjisari
Biographical entry for Alaa al-Din Ali al-Qawjisari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly journey and contributions of Alaa al-Din Ali al-Qawjisari as a student of al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif.

Core Idea
A scholar's travels and teachers shape his legacy.

This lesson introduces you to a lesser-known but significant scholar from the 8th century AH. Alaa al-Din Ali al-Qawjisari was a student of two giants of Islamic scholarship: al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif. His biography, as recorded in al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya, illustrates the scholarly networks that spanned from Persia to Anatolia.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of al-Qawjisari's life and achievements.
Notice the structure: studies, travels, teachers, works, and estimation of his death.
2
Identify the key figures
Identify the names of scholars mentioned: al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif. Who were they? Reflect on their stature.
These are major figures in Islamic theology and rhetoric.
3
Analyze the work mentioned
Focus on his gloss (hashiya) on al-Taftazani's commentary on al-Miftah. Why does the source praise it?
It shows his skill in Arabic sciences.
4
Reflect on the historical context
Consider the significance of his travels from 'lands of the non-Arabs' to 'lands of the Romans'. What does this tell about scholarly mobility?
The 8th century AH was a period of scholarly exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦ - علاء الدين علي القوجحصاري: يقول عنه صاحب الشقائق النعمانية: قرأ على علماء عصره ثم ارتحل إلى بلاد العجم وقرأ على العلامة التفتازاني، والسيد الشريف، ثم ارتحل إلى بلاد الروم. وفي تلك البلاد البعيدة فوض إليه تدريس بعض المواد في إحدى المدارس وصنف بعض الكتب منها: ١ - حاشية على شرح المفتاح للعلامة التفتازاني. ويتابع صاحب الشقائق حديثه بقوله: ويفهم من تلك الحاشية أن له مهارة تامة في العلوم العربية، لأنها حاشية مقبولة أورد فيها تحقيقات كثيرة. ولم يورد صاحب الشقائق شيئاً لا من قريب ولا من بعيد عن حياته وتاريخ مولده ووفاته. وإن كان تاريخ الوفاة يكاد يكون على وجه التقريب في النصف الأول من القرن الثامن الهجري رحمه الله (۲).
6 - Alaa al-Din Ali al-Qawjisari: The author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya says about him: He studied under the scholars of his time, then traveled to the lands of the non-Arabs and studied under the eminent scholar al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif, then traveled to the lands of the Romans. And in those distant lands, he was entrusted with teaching some subjects in one of the schools, and he authored some books, among them: 1 - A gloss on the commentary on al-Miftah by the eminent scholar al-Taftazani. The author of al-Shaqa'iq continues his account saying: It is understood from that gloss that he had perfect skill in the Arabic sciences, because it is an acceptable gloss in which he presented many investigations. And the author of al-Shaqa'iq did not mention anything, near or far, about his life or his date of birth and death. However, the date of death is approximately in the first half of the eighth century AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Alaa al-Din Ali al-Qawjisari, based on al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. It states that he studied under scholars of his time, then travelled to the lands of the non-Arabs (Iran/Transoxiana) and studied under al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani. Then he travelled to the lands of the Romans (Anatolia). There he was assigned to teach some subjects in a school, and he authored several works. One of his known works is a gloss (hashiya) on al-Taftazani's commentary on al-Miftah (a work on rhetoric). The source notes that this gloss demonstrates his mastery of Arabic sciences, as it is a well-accepted gloss containing many investigations. The biography concludes by noting that no details of his life or dates are given, but his death is estimated in the first half of the 8th century AH (14th century CE).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Qawjisari's name is read as al-Kujahsari.

Lineage Dispute in Muhammad Ataullah's Biography
Biographical entry with a note on lineage dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic biographers recorded disagreements about lineage and the importance of such disputes in historical context.

Core Idea
Lineage disputes reveal the care scholars took in preserving accurate historical records.

In Islamic biographical literature, recording a scholar's lineage was a matter of great importance. However, when sources conflicted, biographers would note the disagreement rather than suppress it. This brief entry on Muhammad Ataullah illustrates that practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage along with its translation. Notice the precise wording indicating a clear difference of opinion.
2
Identify the disagreement
The text states there was a clear disagreement about his lineage. One version of his lineage is given: Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Imam Fakhr al-Din Muhammad ibn Umar.
The passage does not provide the alternative lineage, only one version.
3
Consider why lineage mattered
Reflect on the importance of lineage in Islamic scholarship for establishing identity, credibility, and connections between scholars.
Lineage could affect a scholar's reputation and the transmission of knowledge.
4
Reflect on scholarly honesty
The biographer's honesty in recording the dispute shows a commitment to accuracy over simplicity.
This practice is common in Islamic biographical works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧ - محمد عطاء الله بن محمد: اختلف في نسبه اختلافاً بيناً فقيل بعد ذلك هو أحمد بن محمود بن الإمام فخر الدين محمد بن عمر.
7 - Muhammad Ataullah ibn Muhammad: There was a clear difference of opinion regarding his lineage, for it was said after that he is Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Imam Fakhr al-Din Muhammad ibn Umar.

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical entry for Muhammad Ataullah ibn Muhammad. It notes that there is a clear disagreement about his lineage: some say he is Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Imam Fakhr al-Din Muhammad ibn Umar. The rest of the entry is missing or not provided in the scanned pages.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage shows a biographer openly recording uncertainty. In what areas of your own faith or life do you avoid acknowledging uncertainty because it feels uncomfortable? What would change if you embraced that discomfort as a path to deeper knowledge?
?
Think of a time you were unsure about the accuracy of a religious claim. Did you investigate further or simply dismiss it? What can this scholar's willingness to record disagreement teach you about your own responsibility to seek truth even when answers are not clear?

Concludes a biography with patronage, conflict, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concluding events of a scholar's life, including patronage, conflict, and death details from a historical biography.

Core Idea
A scholar's life concludes with honor, a political rift, and a recorded death.

This passage is the final part of a biography. It recounts how the scholar was honored by a ruler, later fell out with another, eventually headed a religious institute, and died after illness. The details provide a window into medieval scholarly life and patronage.

Guided Path

Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the names and key terms.

The passage covers four main events: honoring by al-Ashraf, conflict with al-Zahir Jaqmaq, appointment as shaykh of Qubbat al-Nasr, and death with burial details. List them.
Pay attention to the sequence and the precise date.
3

Consider why such details are recorded: they preserve the scholar's legacy, show the relationship between scholars and rulers, and provide historical chronology.
This type of biographical entry is common in Islamic historical and biographical dictionaries.

He resided there until a prolonged illness, and died on Monday, 11 Rabi' al-Awwal 854 H (around 1450 CE) at about seventy years of age, buried at Bab al-Wazir.
