Life of Imam al-Taftazani
beginner
5 min
Further Students: Sa'd al-Din Lar, Qara Dawud, and Fath Allah al-Shirwani
Biographical entries for three more scholars connected to al-Taftazani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical challenges and achievements of three more of al-Taftazani's associates: Sa'd al-Din Lar, Qara Dawud, and Fath Allah al-Shirwani.

Core Idea
Some students of al-Taftazani are barely known despite their scholarly contributions.

This lesson covers three more entries from the biographical series. The first, Sa'd al-Din Lar, is only mentioned indirectly. The second, Qara Dawud, is known for his glosses but his dates are lost. The third, Fath Allah al-Shirwani, is well-documented as a student of both al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani.

Guided Path
1
Read the three entries
Read the Arabic and translation for entries 16, 17, and 18. Notice the varying amounts of information for each scholar.
2
Note the sources cited
Observe which biographical works are referenced for each entry: al-Sakhawi, Kashf al-Zunun, al-Shaqa'iq, etc.
3
Compare the levels of detail
Entry 16 is very brief, entry 17 includes a gloss but no dates, entry 18 is more complete.
4
Reflect on the author's commentary
Note the author's lament about the difficulty of heritage research in entry 17.

Commentary
This passage is a series of six biographical entries from the introduction of Sharh al-Maqasid, listing scholars connected to al-Taftazani. The author (the editor or commentator) provides what is known about each figure, often citing sources. The passage proceeds in numerical order:

1. Entry 13 (Shihab al-Din Muhammad): The author notes that this person is mentioned by al-Laknawi in his biography of al-Jami as having attended lessons of Shihab al-Din Muhammad, a student of al-Taftazani. Despite extensive research, no further biographical details are found.

2. Entry 14 (Shams al-Din al-Fanari): Full name given as Muhammad ibn Hamzah, a Hanafi judge. He was knowledgeable in Arabic and semantics; born 751 AH. His grandson's biography indicates he was from Transoxiana and a student of al-Taftazani. The author adds that some researchers credit al-Fanari with a crucial role in promoting al-Taftazani's works: he added Monday to the weekly holidays (Friday and Tuesday) to allow students to copy the books, which were not available for purchase.

3. Entry 15 (al-Athir al-Baghdadi): Quoting al-Sakhawi's al-Daw' al-Lami', he is identified as Jibril ibn Salih. He studied under al-Taftazani, and Mahmud ibn al-'Ayni read to him works like al-Mufassal and al-Tawdih with al-Tanqih. Al-Sakhawi remains silent about his birth and death, possibly because he only meant to include notables of the ninth century.

4. Entry 16 (Sa'd al-Din Lar): No biography found; not mentioned in al-Taftazani's history. However, al-Sakhawi in his biography of al-Kirmani lists him as a distinguished teacher who was a student of al-Taftazani.

5. Entry 17 (Qara Dawud): Mentioned by Katib Çelebi in Kashf al-Zunun concerning al-Jurjani. He wrote a gloss on Qutb al-Din al-Tahtani's Sharh al-Shamsiyyah, which itself has many glosses, including one by Qara Dawud. Neither al-Nujum al-Zahirah nor al-Daw' al-Lami' mention him, so his dates are unknown. The author reflects on the difficulty of such research.

6. Entry 18 (Fath Allah al-Shirwani): Agreed upon as Fath Allah ibn 'Abd Allah, a Hanafi. He studied under both al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani, benefiting in intellectual and legal sciences. Among his works is a commentary on Irshad al-Hadi in grammar. The footnotes cite sources for each entry.

Checkpoint
Which of the following scholars studied under both al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani?
A) Sa'd al-Din Lar
B) Qara Dawud
C) Fath Allah al-Shirwani
D) Shihab al-Din Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The survival of biographical information for scholars is uneven; even students of great teachers may remain obscure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about scholars from Islamic history, do you assume that those with long biographies were the only ones who mattered? What would happen to your own legacy if it were reduced to a single line in a book?
?
The author says the hardship of heritage research is only truly appreciated by those who have suffered it. Have you ever felt frustrated trying to learn the details of a scholar or text? How does that frustration change your gratitude for those who preserved knowledge for you?
?
If your name were to be forgotten except for a brief mention in a teacher's biography, would that be enough for you? What does that say about your true intention in seeking knowledge—is it for recognition or for the sake of Allah?

Life of Imam al-Taftazani
beginner
4 min
Biography of Sa'd al-Din Lar
Records a student of al-Taftazani with limited biographical information.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how biographical information about lesser-known scholars is preserved through indirect references in larger biographical works.

Core Idea
Even sparse biographical traces reveal scholarly networks and chains of learning.

This lesson examines a brief note about Sa'd al-Din Lar, a student of the famous scholar al-Taftazani. Although no independent biography survives, the 15th-century historian al-Sakhawi preserves a reference in his biography of another scholar. This small passage teaches us how historical knowledge often depends on indirect sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the specific details: no biography exists, not in Taftazani's history, but al-Sakhawi mentions him.
This is a short, factual entry.
2
Identify the source of information
The only known reference comes from al-Sakhawi's biography of Abu al-Hasan Ali al-Kirmani. Understand how that reference connects Lar to Taftazani.
3
Reflect on historical gaps
Consider why a biography might not survive for this scholar despite his connection to famous figures. This highlights the fragmentary nature of historical records.
4
Appreciate the value of indirect sources
Even a single line from a secondary source can confirm a student-teacher relationship and help reconstruct scholarly chains (isnads).
This is important for understanding how Islamic knowledge was transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سعد الدين لر : وهذا لم نعثر له على ترجمة، ولم يذكر في تاريخ التفتازاني، ولكن يذكره السخاوي في ترجمة أبي الحسن علي الكرماني على أنه من شيوخه الفضلاء فقال : وقال : ومن شيوخه سعد الدين لر الذي كان من طلبة التفتازاني )
Sa'd al-Din Lar: We did not find a biography for him, and he is not mentioned in the history of al-Taftazani, but al-Sakhawi mentions him in his biography of Abu al-Hasan Ali al-Kirmani as one of his virtuous teachers. He said: 'And among his teachers was Sa'd al-Din Lar, who was a student of al-Taftazani.'
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical note on Sa'd al-Din Lar. The author states that no independent biography for him exists, and he is absent from al-Taftazani's own biographical history. However, al-Sakhawi references him while discussing Abu al-Hasan Ali al-Kirmani, describing Sa'd al-Din Lar as one of al-Kirmani's virtuous teachers. Al-Sakhawi further quotes that Lar was a student of al-Taftazani, confirming his place in al-Taftazani's circle despite the scarcity of personal details.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Scholars with famous teachers always have detailed biographies.
Correction: Many scholars, like Sa'd al-Din Lar, are known only through scattered references despite having notable teachers.

Checkpoint
How is Sa'd al-Din Lar's connection to al-Taftazani known?
A) From al-Taftazani's own history.
B) From al-Sakhawi's biography of Abu al-Hasan Ali al-Kirmani.
C) From a dedicated biography of Lar.
D) From al-Sakhawi's biography of al-Taftazani.

Key Takeaway
Even minimal biographical traces can confirm scholarly connections and help reconstruct chains of transmission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you consider the names and sacrifices of the scholars who transmitted the knowledge you now have? Are you actively grateful for this chain?
?
If your entire legacy were reduced to one sentence in a biographical dictionary, what would that sentence say about your relationship to Islamic knowledge? Does that challenge you to deepen your study?
?
The passage shows that even a person without an independent biography can be a vital link in the chain of learning. Are you content to be a hidden link, or do you seek recognition? How does this shape your intention in seeking knowledge?

The Elusive Biography of Qara Dawud
Biographical note highlighting difficulty in dating Qara Dawud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difficulties in dating certain classical scholars due to the lack of biographical records, exemplified by the case of Qara Dawud.

Core Idea
Biographical gaps challenge even the best researchers.

This brief biographical passage introduces Qara Dawud, a student of al-Taftazani known for a gloss on Sharh al-Shamsiyya. The author highlights a common struggle in Islamic intellectual history: many scholars from the tradition remain elusive because major biographical works do not mention them. By examining this example, we see how the lack of records prevents us from establishing even basic details like birth and death dates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures mentioned
Notice that Qara Dawud is a student of al-Taftazani and is mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun in relation to al-Jurjani. This links him to a chain of scholarship.
2
Understand the significance of the gloss
Qara Dawud wrote a gloss on Sharh al-Shamsiyya, which itself attracted many superglosses. This indicates the importance and influence of his work, even if his personal history is obscure.
3
Reflect on the researcher's difficulty
The author laments that neither al-Nujum al-Zahira nor al-Daw’ al-Lami’ mention him, making dating impossible. Reflect on why such gaps occur and how they affect our understanding of intellectual history.
This is the central point of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قره داود (۲) ذكره صاحب كتاب كشف الظنون عند ذكره للسيد الشريف الجرجاني، (۳) له حاشية على شرح الشمسية لقطب الدين التحتاني، وعلى هذه الحاشية حواشي كثيرة منها : حاشية للمولى قره دواد من تلامذة سعد الدين التفتازاني ولم يذكره صاحب النجوم الزاهرة، ولا صاحب الضوء اللامع، وبذلك لا يمكن تحديد تاريخ ولادته أو وفاته، وهذه الحيرة التي يعيش فيها الباحث الذي يتعامل مع كتب التراث لا يقدرها حق قدرها إلا من عاش مثل هذه المعاناة .
Qara Dawud (2): The author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned him when mentioning al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani. (3) He wrote a gloss on Sharh al-Shamsiyya by Qutb al-Din al-Tahtani, and on this gloss there are many superglosses, among them a gloss by al-Mawla Qara Dawud, a student of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. Sahib al-Nujum al-Zahira and Sahib al-Daw' al-Lami' did not mention him, and thus it is impossible to determine his birth or death date. This confusion in which the researcher who deals with heritage books lives cannot be appreciated except by one who has experienced such suffering.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on Qara Dawud. The author identifies him as a student of al-Taftazani and notes that he is mentioned in Kashf al-Zunun in the entry on al-Jurjani. His known work is a gloss on Sharh al-Shamsiyya, itself a commentary by Qutb al-Din al-Tahtani, and that gloss generated many further superglosses. The author laments that neither Ibn Taghribirdi (author of al-Nujum al-Zahira) nor al-Sakhawi (author of al-Daw' al-Lami') mention Qara Dawud, making it impossible to determine his dates. The passage ends with a reflection on the difficulties faced by researchers of classical texts.

Key Terms
حاشية
شرح الشمسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the birth and death date of Qara Dawud unknown?
A) He was not a student of al-Taftazani.
B) He wrote no works.
C) Major biographical sources do not mention him.
D) He lived in the 10th century.

Key Takeaway
Even a significant scholar like Qara Dawud can remain historically obscure when major biographical sources omit him, underscoring the challenges of reconstructing the lives of many Islamic scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Qara Dawud's name survived only through a gloss and a mention in a bibliographic work. Imagine something you have worked hard on—if it were forgotten except for a footnote, would you consider your effort wasted? Why or why not? How does this shape your view of seeking knowledge solely for Allah's sake?
?
The author says only those who have experienced the frustration of missing sources can truly appreciate it. Think of a time you desperately needed information but couldn't find it. Did you persist or give up? How does that experience help you empathize with the researchers who struggle to piece together Islamic history?
?
If you were to disappear from all records except one obscure reference, what would you want that reference to say about you? Are you living now in a way that would make even that single reference valuable to someone seeking truth?

The Life and Teachers of Fath Allah al-Shirwani
Biographical entry on a student of al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage and contributions of the Hanafi scholar Fath Allah al-Shirwani, including his teachers, works, and death date.

Core Idea
Fath Allah al-Shirwani was a direct student of two giants: al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani.

Biographies of scholars help us trace the transmission of knowledge. In this lesson, we meet Fath Allah al-Shirwani, a Hanafi scholar who studied under two of the most famous minds of his era: al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani. The passage gives us his identity, his teachers, his own scholarly work, and the year of his death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his sources
Read how the passage first establishes his identity by citing two biographical works. Notice the full name and affiliation (Hanafi, from Shirwan).
Al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya and Miftah al-Sa'ada are the sources.
2
Trace his teachers
The passage lists two teachers: al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani. Ask: why are these names significant in Islamic scholarship?
Both are major figures in kalam and logic.
3
Examine his scholarly output
It mentions a commentary on Irshad al-Hadi, a grammar work by al-Taftazani. Consider what this tells us about his specialization.
4
Note the death date
The year 857 AH provides a chronological anchor. Reflect on how biographies often end with death dates to place scholars in time.
This helps in studying chains of transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو فتح الله الشرواني تتفق الشقائق النعمانية، ومفتاح السعادة في أنه فتح الله بن عبد الله الشرواني الرومي الحنفي. أخذ عن العلامة التفتازاني ، والسيد الشريف الجرجاني، واستفاد منهما العلوم العقلية والشرعية. ومن تصانيفه شرح كتاب إرشاد الهادي في النحو للعلامة سعد الدين التفتازاني وغيره . وتوفي سنة ٨٥٧ هـ
He is Fath Allah al-Shirwani. Al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya and Miftah al-Sa'ada agree that he is Fath Allah ibn Abd Allah al-Shirwani al-Rumi al-Hanafi. He studied under al-'Allama al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani, and benefited from them in the rational and religious sciences. Among his works is a commentary on the book Irshad al-Hadi in grammar by al-'Allama Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and others. He died in the year 857 AH.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Fath Allah al-Shirwani. It first establishes his identity by citing two biographical works that agree on his full name and affiliation (Hanafi, from Shirwan). Then it lists his teachers: al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani, from whom he acquired both rational and religious sciences. His scholarly output is exemplified by a commentary on al-Taftazani's own work, Irshad al-Hadi, which is a grammar text. Finally, his death date is given as 857 AH, providing a clear chronological anchor.

Key Terms
فتح الله الشرواني
العلامة
السيد الشريف
العلوم العقلية
العلوم الشرعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which two famous scholars did Fath Allah al-Shirwani study?
A) Qutb al-Din al-Tahtani and al-Sakhawi.
B) Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani.
C) Ibn Taghribirdi and al-Sakhawi.
D) Only al-Taftazani.

Key Takeaway
Fath Allah al-Shirwani was a Hanafi scholar who studied under al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani, authored a commentary on Irshad al-Hadi, and died in 857 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have teachers and mentors in your life. Are you genuinely benefiting from them in both rational knowledge (like logic, analysis) and religious knowledge? What is one concrete step this week to integrate both?
?
Fath Allah al-Shirwani didn't just learn—he wrote a commentary on his teacher's work. What knowledge have you received that you could build upon or teach others? What is stopping you from becoming a producer of knowledge, not just a consumer?
?
Consider the names of your greatest intellectual influences. Do you merely admire them from afar, or have you truly sat at their feet and absorbed their teachings? What change in your approach is needed to move from distant admirer to direct student?

The Scant Biography of Mahmud al-Sara'i
Notes the lack of biographical data for a student of al-Taftazani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the limited biographical information available for some scholars like Mahmud al-Sara'i and how modern researchers rely on secondary sources.

Core Idea
Sometimes all we know is a name and a teacher.

Historical research often confronts frustrating gaps. In this short passage, we see how even a major figure like al-Taftazani's student Mahmud al-Sara'i may be known only from a passing mention in his grandson's biography. This lesson explores the challenge of piecing together a scholar's life from scant clues.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two pieces of information: his name and that he studied under al-Taftazani.
Also note the footnote marker.
2
Identify the source
The source is al-Sakhawi's al-Daw' al-Lami'. Why is it significant?
Al-Sakhawi is a famous historian.
3
Consider the limitation
The author points out that al-Sakhawi rarely provides chronological details. Think about why this matters for historical research.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محمود السرائي : ذكره الإمام السخاوي في ترجمة يوسف بن الحسن بن محمود السرائي حيث قال : وجده محمود قيل : ممن أخذ عن سعد الدين التفتازاني وغيره (۲) . وكعادة صاحب الضوء اللامع أنه في أغلب الأوقات لا يقدم لنا تاريخاً يعطي ضوءاً على حياته ونوراً يكشف عن جوانب شخصيته
Mahmud al-Sara'i: Imam al-Sakhawi mentioned him in the biography of Yusuf ibn al-Hasan ibn Mahmud al-Sara'i, where he said: 'His grandfather Mahmud is said to have studied under Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and others (2). And, as is the habit of the author of al-Daw' al-Lami', most of the time he does not provide us with a history that sheds light on his life or a light that reveals aspects of his personality.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on Mahmud al-Sara'i. The only known information comes from al-Sakhawi's al-Daw' al-Lami' in the entry on his grandson Yusuf. Al-Sakhawi reports that Mahmud is said to have studied under al-Taftazani and others. The author then notes a characteristic of al-Sakhawi's work: often it does not provide sufficient chronological or personal details about the subjects. Thus, this entry highlights the frustration of relying on a source that is sometimes incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who mentions Mahmud al-Sara'i, and in what context?
A) The author of Kashf al-Zunun in the entry on al-Jurjani.
B) Al-Sakhawi in the biography of his grandson Yusuf.
C) Ibn Taghribirdi in al-Nujum al-Zahira.
D) Al-Taftazani in his own history.

Key Takeaway
Even a single hearsay mention can be the only record of a scholar's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that all we have of Mahmud al-Sara'i is a name and a hearsay, do you realize that your own legacy may be just as bare? What are you doing today to ensure that the knowledge you carry is passed on with more detail than a 'qila'?
?
Al-Sakhawi often omitted dates and details. In your own learning, have you been content to know a scholar only by name? How can you take responsibility for digging deeper into the lives of those you study from, so that their full contribution is not lost?
?
The passage states that 'most of the time he does not provide us with a history.' Does this prompt you to be more deliberate in recording your own teachers and their teachings? What specific step will you take this week to document something about a scholar you have learned from?

Al-Taftazani's Enduring Legacy: Direct and Indirect Students
Summarizes the impact of al-Taftazani's teaching through direct and indirect students.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani's teaching reached scholars through both direct oral instruction and the influence of his written works.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's school lives on through both his students and his books.

This passage concludes the biographical sketch of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani by reflecting on his vast influence. The author highlights two circles of students: those who studied directly with him, and a much larger group across the East and West who learned through his writings. The passage presents his legacy as an enduring school of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's tone of appreciation and the two distinct groups described.
2
Identify the two groups
The passage mentions direct students who sat before al-Taftazani and received oral instruction, and indirect students who studied through his books. Underline the phrases that describe each group.
The signal phrase 'But there are huge groups' marks the transition.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how a scholar's written works can extend their influence far beyond their lifetime and geography. Think about why the author calls this 'a school rich in knowledge'.
This connects to the learning objective about enduring legacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد فهذه مجموعة من العمالقة ممن تتلمذوا على سعد الدين التفتازاني حيث جلسوا بين يديه وتلقوا منه العلم مشافهة واستمعوا إلى حديثه، وتداولوا معه أطراف العلم، وألوان المعرفة . ولكن هناك مجموعات ضخمة من الأساتذة والمفكرين في العالم الغربي والشرقي تتلمذوا على كتبه ونهلوا من ينابيعه وكانت لهم زادا في إعدادهم العلمي، وتكوينهم الفكري . إنها مدرسة غنية بالمعرفة ثرية بالعطاء، وستستمر عبر التاريخ حتى يرث الله الأرض ومن عليها
After this, these are a group of giants who studied under Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, sitting before him, receiving knowledge orally, listening to his discourse, and exchanging with him the branches of knowledge and kinds of wisdom. But there are huge groups of teachers and thinkers in the Western and Eastern worlds who studied through his books and drank from his springs, and they were a provision in their scientific preparation and intellectual formation. It is a school rich in knowledge, abundant in giving, and it will continue throughout history until Allah inherits the earth and those upon it.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a concluding reflection on the legacy of al-Taftazani as a teacher. The author distinguishes two types of students: first, those who studied directly with al-Taftazani in person, described as giants who sat at his feet, received oral instruction, and engaged in scholarly exchange. Second, an even larger group of scholars and thinkers across the East and West who learned from his written works, which served as a foundation for their own education and thought. The author presents al-Taftazani's intellectual tradition as an enduring school that will persist until the end of time.

Key Terms
تلمذ على
مشافهة
ينابيعه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the passage describe the second group of al-Taftazani's students?
A) They studied directly with him.
B) They learned through his books.
C) They were only from the East.
D) They were few in number.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's legacy persists through both his direct students and the countless scholars who continue to learn from his writings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You benefit from scholars you have never met through their books. What responsibility does that place on you to preserve and transmit what you learn?
?
If your knowledge were to end with you, would you be satisfied? What can you do today to ensure your learning benefits others beyond your lifetime?
?
Al-Taftazani's school continues through his writings. Are you merely consuming knowledge, or are you preparing to pass it on? What is one concrete step you will take to become a source of benefit for others?

Life of Imam al-Taftazani

Al-Taftazani's Students and His Enduring Legacy
Biographical note on Mahmud al-Sira'i and concluding remarks on al-Taftazani's school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of al-Taftazani's scholarly legacy, including his direct students and the broader influence of his writings.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's legacy extends beyond direct students to generations of scholars who studied his books.

In this concluding passage, the author reflects on the students of al-Taftazani, both those who sat before him and those who learned from his writings. The passage highlights the enduring impact of his school of thought, citing a specific biographical example and then expanding to a global influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify its two main sections
The passage begins with a specific reference to Mahmud al-Sira'i and then broadens to a general reflection on al-Taftazani's students and legacy. Notice the shift in scope.
Pay attention to the citation from al-Sakhawi.
2
Understand the biographical note on Mahmud al-Sira'i
The passage cites Imam al-Sakhawi, who mentions that Mahmud al-Sira'i was among those who studied under al-Taftazani. This shows the chain of transmission.
Al-Sakhawi's work al-Daw' al-Lami' is the source.
3
Recognize the distinction between direct and indirect students
The author highlights two groups: those who sat before al-Taftazani and received knowledge orally, and those who studied his books across the Eastern and Western worlds.
This emphasizes the widespread influence of his writings.
4
Reflect on the concluding statement about the school's endurance
The passage ends by describing al-Taftazani's school as rich and enduring until the end of time. Consider why the author chooses this tone.
This serves as a testament to his lasting impact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للعلامة سعد الدين التفتازاني وغيره . وتوفي سنة ٨٥٧ هـ (١)
۱۹ - محمود السرائي :
ذكره الإمام السخاوي في ترجمة يوسف بن الحسن بن محمود السرائي حيث قال : وجده محمود قيل : ممن أخذ عن سعد الدين التفتازاني وغيره (۲) . وكعادة صاحب الضوء اللامع أنه في أغلب الأوقات لا يقدم لنا تاريخاً يعطي ضوءاً على حياته ونوراً يكشف عن جوانب شخصيته (۳)
وبعد فهذه مجموعة من العمالقة ممن تتلمذوا على سعد الدين التفتازاني حيث جلسوا بين يديه وتلقوا منه العلم ،مشافهة واستمعوا إلى حديثه، وتداولوا معه أطراف العلم، وألوان المعرفة .
ولكن هناك مجموعات ضخمة من الأساتذة والمفكرين في العالم الغربي والشرقي تتلمذوا على كتبه ونهلوا من ينابيعه وكانت لهم زادا في إعدادهم العلمي، وتكوينهم الفكري .
إنها مدرسة غنية بالمعرفة ثرية بالعطاء، وستستمر عبر التاريخ حتى يرث الله الأرض ومن عليها
(۱) راجع كتاب كشف الظنون ج ١ ص ٦٧ ومفتاح السعادة ج ١ ص ٢٠٦ . والشقائق النعمانية
ج ۱ ص ۱۷۰.
(۲) راجع الضوء اللامع ج ۱۰ ص ۳۱۰ .
(۳) المرجع السابق ج ۱۰ ص ۳۱۲ .
For the scholar Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and others. And he died in the year 857 AH (1).
19 - Mahmud al-Sira'i:
Imam al-Sakhawi mentioned him in the biography of Yusuf ibn al-Hasan ibn Mahmud al-Sira'i, where he said: 'His grandfather Mahmud, it is said, was among those who took [knowledge] from Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and others (2).' And as is the custom of the author of al-Daw' al-Lami', that most of the time he does not provide us with a history that sheds light on his life and a light that reveals aspects of his personality (3).
After this, these are a group of giants who studied under Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, sitting before him, receiving knowledge from him orally, listening to his discourse, and exchanging with him the various branches and colors of knowledge.
But there are huge groups of professors and thinkers in the Western and Eastern worlds who studied his books, drank from his springs, and they were provisions in their academic preparation and intellectual formation.
Indeed, it is a school rich in knowledge, abundant in giving, and will continue throughout history until Allah inherits the earth and those upon it.
(1) See Kashf al-Zunun, vol. 1, p. 67, and Miftah al-Sa'ada, vol. 1, p. 206, and al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya, vol. 1, p. 170.
(2) See al-Daw' al-Lami', vol. 10, p. 310.
(3) Ibid., vol. 10, p. 312.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note and concluding remark about the students and legacy of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. It first mentions Mahmud al-Sira'i, citing the authority of Imam al-Sakhawi, who in his biography of Yusuf ibn al-Hasan ibn Mahmud al-Sira'i reports that the grandfather, Mahmud, was said to have studied under al-Taftazani and others. The passage notes that al-Sakhawi, as is his custom in al-Daw' al-Lami', often does not provide detailed biographical dates or insights. Then the author steps back and reflects: these are some of the giants who studied directly under al-Taftazani, sitting before him, receiving knowledge orally, and engaging in scholarly exchange. Beyond direct students, there are vast numbers of scholars in both the East and West who studied his books and drew from his intellectual springs, which became provisions for their own academic and intellectual development. The passage concludes by describing the Taftazani school as rich in knowledge, abundant in giving, and enduring until Allah inherits the earth.

Key Terms
سعد الدين التفتازاني
محمود السرائي
السخاوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is about al-Taftazani's own life.
Correction: The passage primarily discusses his students and the influence of his works, not his biography.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is said about Mahmud al-Sira'i?
A) He was a teacher of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani.
B) He was a student of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani according to al-Sakhawi.
C) He wrote the book al-Daw' al-Lami'.
D) He died in the year 857 AH.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's scholarly legacy includes both his direct students and countless others who benefited from his writings, ensuring his school's continuity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your entire legacy were reduced to what you have learned and passed on to others, what would remain after you? Are you investing in knowledge that will outlive you?
?
The direct students sat before al-Taftazani and received knowledge orally. Today, you have access to his books and lectures. Do you approach your learning with the same reverence and hunger as if you were sitting at the feet of a living master? What would change if you did?
?
The passage says al-Taftazani's school will continue 'until Allah inherits the earth.' Your own knowledge—what you study and internalize—has the potential to benefit generations you will never meet. What is one concrete action you will take this week to ensure your learning becomes a lasting spring for others?

Al-Taftazani's Scholarly Status and Acclaim
Biographical notes praising al-Taftazani's scholarly status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Taftazani is regarded as a towering figure in Islamic scholarship, based on the praise of Ibn Taghri Bardi and Ibn Khaldun.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani's scholarly acclaim sets the stage for the authority of his commentary.

Before diving into the doctrinal content of Sharh al-Maqasid, it's important to appreciate the stature of its author. This brief biographical passage introduces us to al-Taftazani through the eyes of two renowned historians, Ibn Taghri Bardi and Ibn Khaldun. Their testimonies establish his mastery across both rational and transmitted sciences, lending weight to his theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the full meaning of the text.
Notice the enthusiastic tone of praise right from the opening.
2
Identify the two authorities quoted
Look for the names Ibn Taghri Bardi and Ibn Khaldun. What specific achievements do they highlight about al-Taftazani?
Both historians emphasize his mastery in rational sciences (al-ma'qul) and transmitted sciences (al-manqul).
3
Reflect on the purpose of this biography
Ask yourself why the author includes this praise at the beginning of a theological commentary. How does this establish trust in the author's authority?
This is a common feature in classical Islamic scholarship: the author's credentials are established early to assure the reader of the work's reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكانته العلمية
ورأي العلماء فيه
عملاق
من عمالقة الفكر، ورائد من رواد المعرفة، وشيخ أطبقت شهرته
على الآفاق، وتخطت السدود والحدود. يصفه ابن تغري بردى فيقول :
كان فريد عصره ووحيده دهره وإنه برع في المعقول، وساد على أقرانه، وشارك في المنقول وفي أنواع من العلوم وتصدى للإقراء والتدريس، وبرع في التأليف والتصنيف، وانتفع بمؤلفاته وبمصنفاته الخاص والعام» (۱)
وقد عرف ابن خلدون فضل التفتازاني، واطلع على مصنفاته في علم البيان والكلام وأصول الفقه ووصفه بأنه من عظماء هراة ، وأشاد بمكانته في العلوم العقلية، وذلك حيث يقول :
ولقد وقفت بمصر على تأليف متعددة لرجل من عظماء هراة من بلاد خراسان يشهر بسعد الدين التفتازاني، منها في علم الكلام وأصول الفقه والبيان تشهد بأن له ملكة راسخة في هذه العلوم. وفي أثنائها ما يدل على أن له اطلاعاً على العلوم الحكمية، وقدماً عالية في سائر الفنون العقلية» (۲)
أما صاحب كتاب أعلام الأخيار فيصفه بأنه موسوعة علمية، ودائرة معارف في العلوم الإسلامية فهو وإن كان شافعي المذهب، إلا أنه يكتب في فقه
(۱) المنهل الصافي ج ٣ ص ٣٥٦ بتصرف. (۲) راجع مقدمة ابن خلدون ج ۳ ص ۱۰۹۱ .
His scholarly status and the opinion of scholars about him. A giant among the giants of thought, a pioneer among the pioneers of knowledge, a master whose fame covered the horizons and surpassed barriers and borders. Ibn Taghri Bardi describes him, saying: 'He was the unique one of his age and the solitary one of his time, and he excelled in rational sciences, dominated his peers, and participated in transmitted sciences and various types of knowledge. He undertook instruction and teaching, excelled in authorship and composition, and benefited from his works and compositions both the elite and the common.' (1) Ibn Khaldun recognized the merit of al-Taftazani and reviewed his works on rhetoric, theology (kalam), and principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh), and described him as one of the greats of Herat and praised his standing in the rational sciences, saying: 'I have come across in Cairo multiple works by a man from the greats of Herat, a land of Khorasan, known as Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, among them works on theology, principles of jurisprudence, and rhetoric, which testify that he has a firmly rooted mastery in these sciences. And in them there is evidence that he has knowledge of the philosophical sciences and a high standing in all rational arts.' (2) As for the author of the book ‘A‘lam al-Akhyar’, he describes him as a scientific encyclopedia and a circle of knowledge in the Islamic sciences, for although he was of the Shafi‘i school, he wrote in jurisprudence...
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section that extols the scholarly status of Sa‘d al-Din al-Taftazani, the author of the work. It begins by declaring him a giant of thought and a pioneer of knowledge whose fame spread far and wide. Then it quotes two authorities: first, Ibn Taghri Bardi, who states that al-Taftazani was unique in his time, excelled in rational sciences, dominated his peers, participated in transmitted sciences, and was prolific in teaching and writing, benefiting both the elite and the common people. Second, Ibn Khaldun, who after reviewing al-Taftazani's works on theology (kalam), principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh), and rhetoric (bayan), testified that he had a firmly rooted mastery in these sciences and also had knowledge of philosophical sciences and a high standing in all rational arts. Finally, the author of ‘A‘lam al-Akhyar’ describes him as a scientific encyclopedia and a circle of knowledge in the Islamic sciences, noting that despite being a Shafi‘i in madhhab, he wrote in jurisprudence (the sentence is cut off in the source). The passage thus establishes al-Taftazani's authority and erudition, which lends weight to the commentary that follows in the book.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's mastery across rational and transmitted sciences, attested by Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Taghri Bardi, establishes his authority as a commentator on theological matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Who are the scholars you look up to? Have you ever examined their credentials or are you blindly following? What would it take for you to be as committed to knowledge as al-Taftazani?
?
Al-Taftazani earned recognition from peers across centuries. Are you building a legacy of knowledge that will be remembered after you? What are you doing today to ensure your learning is thorough and beneficial?
?
Ibn Khaldun personally reviewed al-Taftazani's works before praising him. When you hear praise of a scholar, do you verify for yourself, or do you accept it uncritically? How can you develop the habit of seeking knowledge directly from sources?

Al-Taftazani's Scholarly Stature According to Ibn Taghri Birdi
Ibn Taghri Birdi praises al-Taftazani's scholarly standing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Taghri Birdi described al-Taftazani's comprehensive mastery of both rational and transmitted sciences and his impact on scholars and the public.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani was a unique scholar who mastered both rational and transmitted sciences, benefiting all.

This passage introduces us to the towering figure of al-Taftazani through the eyes of the historian Ibn Taghri Birdi. It highlights his unparalleled status in his time, his excellence in rational sciences, and his contributions to numerous fields. The description is both a tribute and a witness to his lasting influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the heading 'His scholarly standing and the opinion of scholars about him'.
2
Identify the key descriptors
Ibn Taghri Birdi uses several phrases to describe al-Taftazani. List them: 'unique of his time', 'excelled in rational sciences', 'participated in transmitted sciences', 'devoted to teaching and authorship', 'benefited specialist and general alike'.
These descriptors paint a picture of a comprehensive scholar.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why mastering both rational and transmitted sciences is important in Islamic scholarship. How does this description elevate al-Taftazani's status?
This connects to the broader theme of scholarly excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكانته العلمية
ورأي العلماء فيه
عملاق
من عمالقة الفكر، ورائد من رواد المعرفة، وشيخ أطبقت شهرته
على الآفاق، وتخطت السدود والحدود. يصفه ابن تغري بردى فيقول :
كان فريد عصره ووحيده دهره وإنه برع في المعقول، وساد على أقرانه، وشارك في المنقول وفي أنواع من العلوم وتصدى للإقراء والتدريس، وبرع في التأليف والتصنيف، وانتفع بمؤلفاته وبمصنفاته الخاص والعام»
His scholarly standing and the opinion of scholars about him. A giant among giants of thought, a pioneer of knowledge, a master whose fame spread to the horizons and crossed barriers and borders. Ibn Taghri Birdi describes him, saying: He was the unique one of his time and the sole one of his age; he excelled in rational sciences, surpassed his peers, participated in transmitted sciences and in various types of knowledge, devoted himself to teaching and instruction, excelled in authorship and composition, and both the specialist and the general benefited from his works and compositions.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a biographical excerpt praising al-Taftazani. It begins with the heading 'His scholarly standing and the opinion of scholars about him' and calls him a 'giant'. Then it introduces the historian Ibn Taghri Birdi, who provides a comprehensive description: al-Taftazani was unparalleled in his time, master of rational sciences, superior to his contemporaries, and also engaged in transmitted sciences and many other fields. He committed himself to teaching and writing, and his works benefited both elites and laypeople.

Key Terms

ابن تغري بردى
المعقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Taftazani only focused on rational sciences (like logic and theology) and neglected transmitted sciences.
Correction: Ibn Taghri Birdi explicitly states that he 'participated in transmitted sciences and in various types of knowledge', showing he was well-versed in both traditions.

Checkpoint
What does Ibn Taghri Birdi say about al-Taftazani's standing in rational and transmitted sciences?
A) He only excelled in rational sciences.
B) He excelled in rational sciences and also participated in transmitted sciences and other fields.
C) He was a student of Ibn Taghri Birdi.
D) He wrote only in one field of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taghri Birdi's description confirms al-Taftazani's unmatched scholarship across both rational and transmitted sciences, with a lasting impact on all levels of learners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a student of knowledge. Ibn Taghri Birdi says al-Taftazani benefited both the specialist and the general public. Are you content to benefit only yourself, or are you actively seeking to benefit others at every level? What concrete step will you take this week to share what you learn with someone less advanced than you?
?
Al-Taftazani excelled in rational sciences and participated in transmitted sciences. Which of these two areas do you neglect, and why? What specific action will you take to strengthen your weakness?
?
His fame spread to horizons and crossed barriers. You may never be famous, but does your pursuit of knowledge reflect any ambition to master multiple disciplines? What is one skill or science you have been avoiding that you will now commit to learning?
